Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "treatment for contusion", and that is what you do behind the patient who has this disease the hairs which he has on his forehead, then make III cuts on his forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II fingers right in the middle of the forehead downwards towards the nose, and the other II at the II sides above the eyebrows, and beware of the incision of the arteries which are at the II sides above the eyebrows; and move your hand away from the connection of the II jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of III fingers across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then apply the spatumile agut of II parts as this is its form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut which is next to the temple up to the second cut; and peel off all the skin that is between the II cuts on the entire surface that is over the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second, and then extract using this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	so place in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side towards the diseased flesh of the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches what opens from the heart, and then do the same in the middle cut until the other side; and then drain the blood equally, and press the area for the drained blood; then place a wick of old cotton in each cut, and put on cloths wet with wine and oil and salt, and ensure that no hot abscesses come there; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and apply plenty of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the realm of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to anyone comes acute catarrh usually, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burned; and the hair falls out, and on the head there comes sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these accidents that those materials and this catarrh do not come from anywhere else but from many veins, and the most effective cure that there is, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you instruct the patient to lie down on his back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one on the wide temple.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then separate the two edges of the incision and put old cotton and flaxen threads in between; then bind over it cloths moistened with wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; when they are removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that promote granulation.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colofonium, and make a poultice; and administer it to these wounds to quicken flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or insects, or minerals like stone or similar things such as iron; or seeds, such as lentils, beans, peas; or flowing substances such as water and wax and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or flaxseed oil, then perform extraction; and make him sneeze with condysium, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and pull the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Very often the stone comes out by this treatment; and if it does not come out, then perform extraction with fine forceps, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, then perform extraction with a fine needle of small double-edging; and if it does not come out by this means, make a cane from lead and place the head of the cane in the opening of the ear firmly, and plug around the cane with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the cane; then pull it out forcefully, as very often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out by such means, take glue from which birds are taken, and place some instrument that is pointed for this purpose in a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal from all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to split the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come; and the method of splitting is that you first let blood from the cephalic vein according to its strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where the fat hangs; and let the cut be like a crescent until you reach the bone, then remove it as much as possible, and suck quickly with your mouth; and treat until healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and they swell, then administer extraction; and if they cannot come out, then administer the spatulum lightly according to this method:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and to administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with fine tweezers and a suction device, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of fluid that falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use sneezing with condiments first, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same ear where the fluid is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, then take many small stones according to the length of your thumb, thin and light, and heat them slightly by fire; and have the patient place one in the perforation of his ear, and jump up with one foot from another part, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this from stone to stone until all the fluid comes out completely, and thus it will come out entirely; and if you want, take reeds, and put one end in the ear, and the other end press with fire until the softer part of the reed is burned; then do the same with other reeds until all the fluid comes out as we have said with the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small body, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body that can be felt, then use extraction with tweezers; and it is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earworms, when you cure it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if worms appear, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take the reed where there is this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finest end into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck forcefully on the entire reed; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, wrap cotton around the reed as I have said for stones; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven for worm occlusions, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose form is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or brass is narrow below a small opening, and above over for distillation; and to press inside the distillation an instrument of brass well made for this, and if you want take the dropper and wrap around the point properly cotton; then pour your oil or your juice, and what you wish of your medicines in the cane, and the cane be in the ear; then put inside the dropper all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil be distilled into the eardrum; and it smells to the patient inside, and let the distillation be a little warmed by fire so that when you distill in the ear; and beware lest it be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the deafness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born who have no openings in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from a wound, or flesh grown inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes comes perfectly within the ear, so one cannot see it; and sometimes there is too much growth closing off the opening, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When it comes perfectly within the ear so one cannot see it, its healing is difficult in many cases, and for that which can be seen, you must place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage clearly, then work on it with this spatula of such form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting on both the front and back but smooth so that it does not hurt the ear; if the blockage is of flesh grown or part of the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and cut it lightly until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstruction is fully in the ear, then take a fine light scraper and warm it slightly over fire, then place it in the core of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction from which the patient feels difficulty in hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a plug according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is sealed, or take a plug and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol over it; and if you see the ear swollen, then you must remove the plug and replace it with another plug moistened in an ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then clean it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papermakers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ailment that comes from papermakers' eyes when they are moist and then dry, you should stretch them with tweezers and brushes, and cut them out with a spatula from their roots; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not heal from this treatment, then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery and the cauterizer after the incision is worth much; and often they return because something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, in the eyes of patients, there appear things that resemble hailstones in their form and hardness, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail", and it is a collection of moisture thickened above and below the eyelid; the treatment is as follows: take notice if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is easy to know; then cut it widely, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with forceps, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cut it without piercing a little the eyelid, do not worry about the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing more, for ointments will restore it quickly and promote flesh growth.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the earwax is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper, and extend the earwax with tweezers, and cut and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the earwax is cut, then lift out with salty water, and clean the area of what runs down until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that runs down into the webbing of the eyes above, and this happens more to children than to other people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, causing them to have catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie on their faces immediately and sleep thus, with their eyelids under their eyebrows moist, covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your hands and feel the protrusion between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the protrusion from each side, then put it on him; and press with your hands from one part to another so that the protrusion be assembled within the circle; then make a cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula, making a slit as wide, and not larger than the wound you make at the vein opening; and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the protrusion; and in many cases, the protrusion comes out through the slit, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it then in one piece of cloth wrapped between your fingers against the wind, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and beware that you do not insert into the cut, that you do not come all the way to the eyelid, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the abscess does not open at the beginning of the cut, enlarge the cut slightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths with oil and water, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind coal and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the eyelids
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs other than natural ones grow in the eyelids and they are irritated, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the eyelids and leucoma, to the point that it can lead to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment follows four methods: by cautery with fire together, or by astringent medicine according to what was mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and suturing or by cautery, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand; if it is turned, that's good; if not, put a needle through all the thread above; and do this near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull the thread over all the eyelid, and turn it with the razor; then cut in the part below the eyelid, under the attached hairs, along the entire spatiumile cutting from the large tear duct up to the small one; then remove the thread, and put a little tent of cotton and cloth under the eyelid, then stain over the eyelid an enche figure like a myrtle leaf, and it always matters that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to lift the separated eyelid.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And so there are those who need that one cut a great quantity of the parchment according to how soft the parchment is; then cut all the spatula above the II lines that you have marked, and begin from the large eyelid down to the small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the knife in one of the two angles of the eye, then peel it all; then bring together the two edges with a suture of an needle with I thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make dry the excess of threads above the II eyebrows with some sticky things, if you wish to do this; and if not, then have no concern for it, then leave the suture and the threads until III days or IV; then treat the wound without a suture with drying and binding things, because the parchment rises at the closure of the wound and its joining, but the suture is softer (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear; and there is another method: which is to mark the parchment in a shape that is like a myrtle leaf, as we have recounted, III inches apart according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes above the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with thread, and insert it into the figure; and place one thread next to the large eyelid, and the other thread next to the small one, and gather between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have recounted, then join together the two edges of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward: you must use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one case and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and cut inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and as wide as the spatula; and cut at the two ends of both sides where you hold the threads; then join one and the other subtly on top of the paper over the eye, and extract the two canes from both sides properly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is constricted will die, blacken, and wither until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with force, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is sealed, and the paper is lifted, the hairs will not prick anymore; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a subtle needle and put a thread of fine silk through it; then bring together the shoulders and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the case another thread of fine silk briefly, and tie the head of the thread; then place the patient's head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and minute work, then push the needle all through the case to the root of the hair attached, and make it pierce into the paper quickly until you pull it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the case, and put in the case that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the hairs come out all from the case into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the shaft is treated and the hair does not come out with it, you will pull the shaft from below along all the thread that you have put there until the shaft comes out of the upper hole and you see it by the sight of the eye; then you will pull the shaft and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days until the hair burns in its place and flesh grows over; and if the hair is small, attach one long hair from natural hair, and raise it with that which you leave until it is extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pus from the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the pus comes to the eye, it happens in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by the suddenness of a wound, or of a cutting or of a cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work in it is that you split that soldering, and separate its lips, and put linen tents inside, and leave it until it is healed; and it does not befit to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and the ash of water or alcohol and flaxseed should be cooked, and anointings of melted mercury in any of the oils, and wrap a tent around it, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you take heed that it does not heal according to the form it was before; and this work which we have said is nothing but remedies for this disease, that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out two fingers from the flesh; then stretch the flesh above all the needle, and cut it with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the membrane returns according to what is needed, it is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the split, and turn the membrane, and make two splits on the inside of the membrane; let the ends of the two splits be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make one angle so that when they are put together, the shape is like that of a letter named «I griesche»; then remove the flesh according to the sharpness of its sides underneath from what lies under the membrane, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a woolen thread; then cure it as we have said about the medicines that soften, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or a seam or a cautery, then you must make a full cut under the hairs of the membranes, as mentioned before; then separate between the two sides of a bandage, as I have said; and one should perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters devise every means possible to restore the shape to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what is needed for the work and the instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this welding happens to men in such a way that the paper above is welded with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural works, then you must put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with pincers, until you cut what is hardened with a fine spatula, which is not too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear for the spatula to be too sharp and wound the eye; and let your incision, with which you peel off this assembly, be lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and heal all of this assembly, and sometimes make a salty water in the eye, and lift it with sweet water and honey; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and place on the eye wool moistened in egg white; and after the third day use the honey and welding things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but resembles white moisture frozen, so when one touches it with iron and tries to pare it with tweezers, no one can; and both appearances begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient put his head in your hand, then move the eyes; and lift the paper in your hand, then cut the nail with tweezers of small double layer, and stretch it above; then take a needle, and put horse hair or ox hair or cow hair, and strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a little and stick it into the nail, and pierce it all the way through the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the nail that is next to the pupil and sew the silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct all the way with the fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh or tear duct so that by the incision the tear fluid does not come as usual; and sometimes stretch the nail only one inch and with thread, as we have said; then scrape it with the whole spatula above which is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the flesh membrane and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a bit of crushed gall, and with the collar made of litharge, leave it until the next day; then clean it as much as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not firm, and you cannot push the needle in, and the forceps cannot enter, this type of nail-like condition is often treated with medicines; and they grow as I have described in the section, and if you wish to cut it, then operate on the patient’s eye, and take the slightly sharp spatula according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail above subtly, and if you see that it does not thin out and the growth presses in, then drip from your mouth into the eye a collar made of litharge and red collar and crushed gall, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin again the other work according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If any thing does not oppose you in the eye, like a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the eyelid harms the eye with great damage, then suspend it to a lancet and cut away part of it but not all, so tears do not come forth; then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restraining it on the eyelids and turning them inward; it looks like a pomegranate rose. The procedure is that the patient places their head in your lap, then you work on the eyes, cutting away all that flesh with appropriate lancets and holding firmly; then cut away the first layer of flesh, going straight to the scraper until the end, being careful not to injure the eye during the operation. The incision should be like that of a spatula we have mentioned in the section about nail incisions and small forces used for removing scales, as is shown later in this chapter; when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply sea onion juice or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into the eye. Place cotton on the eye with egg white so that it prevents a hot abscess from forming. If something remains and there is heat swelling, and you fear a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until healed. And thus do when such flesh is attached in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless you must lighten the treatment of each weak eye by the natural way; and by the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb can withstand that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Sebel are red veins that cover the eye, and they hinder sight's work and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then necessary first that you check if the eye in which sebel is present is swollen and there is no other disease besides the sebel; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, then suspend those veins for a whole ounce according to his wisdom, and let the ounces be doubled as per this method:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then when you coil those veins subtly with force, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move out of the eye; and beware that you do not injure the eye with the points of the spatulae, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut beyond those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red collyria to corrupt what remains of the seborrhea.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to remove all of it in that hour, then apply a plaster on the eye made of things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and there is no fear of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this method that is mentioned until it is healed; and this is the form of the force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician also calls a fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is reason in it that you cut into the abscess where it should be opened, and draw out all the moisture until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then scrape it all with this instrument whose form is here; it is called "aspre chief," and it should be made of iron to its full length, and pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the area of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is scraped off; and do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the sinus is sealed and flesh grows there, and the core of the boil is sealed, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not renew itself nor become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other method than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the vein according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and with medicinal waters, and when it is uncovered take a drill according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-angled, and the handle should be narrowed up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand one inch away from the eye, then turn the entire drill until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the wind that enters if they hold their hand over their vein; then restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the sinus, the matter goes to the vein; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully opened everywhere and there comes no obstruction to the nerve, nor diminishment, then you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply leeches or cupping without puncturing for suction, then put on the eye a bandage made of wax, aloes, frankincense, and storax, and then close the eye, and plaster over with bandages and cloths; and the method of the cloths is that you take fairly soft cloths, and double each one four times, and then place one over another according to the amount needed by the eye; then tightly bind it above with a hard bandage, and repeat cupping for suction without puncturing; then remove the cups and leave the eye tightly bound day and night, and if the bandages soften, then you must tighten them greatly; then remove the binding after one day and one night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, it is good; if not, then repeat the plastering with cloths and the bandage and leeches and cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the breaking of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the woven cloth, then it opens up, and threads fall out like resin grains, making it astonishing to see; then if you see it cut, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the part underneath all the way to the top, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the edge; and pierce it, leaving the first needle according to the arrangement; then cut at the spot with the double thread and tie one part of the weave around tightly, and hold it well, then remove the needle and apply moistened wool over an egg white; and leave it until the threads fall out with the weave, then treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the weave on both sides with a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great appearance, pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes into perfect part of the eye, and let the white moisture run down the eye, and enter in at once; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing more than white substance gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take his head between both hands, and move it until you see the white come up to your eyes; then fix it so that it does not descend and the light is dispersed, and the patient sees things as usual; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the white is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	so make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and cut on the corneal membrane with the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal membrane and the cornea until the pus comes out; and when it has come out, then distill into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek is boiled and honey, then clean it thoroughly until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing; act according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and cover the healthy eye and hold it very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if the eye is right; then put the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a hair on that swelling of the eye at the part of the lesser lacrimal; then forcefully insert the instrument called "almagda" and turn your hand until it pierces into the swelling of the eye, feeling that almagda comes to the empty place; and the measure of the path almagda should be perfectly equal to the space from the pupil to the end of the black part; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, then put the instrument until where the water is, then press it below one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the aqueous humor is now deficient, the patient sees something before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, if the aqueous humor rises through the second passage, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and does not rise, then gently extract almagda by turning your hand little by little; and then reintroduce a bit of seal gem into the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye tufts or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white, and bind with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply ground cumin mixed with egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable sleep, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head to right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this at the time of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary to lighten this, because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses of heat come, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and apply what soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then unbind the sight and put on his face an orilliet to cover for some days, and be thus in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then let him leave the house little by little, and return to his usual activities; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Irach, who told us that in his country they make almagda pierced, to which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any of this in our land, nor have I read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, for those who do not understand them see them; and they are properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of the axes of this same fineness, and the back in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh grows on the nose in various shapes, of which some resemble scorpions with many legs; and there are such cases where the flesh is stained with a fox-colored hue, and it has good-colored swine-like flesh.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case, then, of this flesh which is swine-like and not stained, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and work his nostrils, and throw on some uncinatum to that flesh, and drag it hard; then cut what you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of this flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains something that one cannot cut, then open it all with subtle and light instruments so that nothing remains; and if the blood overflows or the abscess is hot, then help it as appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood is stopped and all the pus is removed, then apply a soft and moist dressing with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the dressing works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healing; and if moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is pus formed in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach to cut: then it is necessary to put a thread of linen slightly thickened, and be knotted by hand, with about one inch or less between each knot; and have the patient place the head of the thread in his nose as far as possible, and pull through smelling until it comes from the nose into the mouth; and this is often done by schoolchildren, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then hold one end that comes out the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out the mouth with the other hand, and unravel one after the other at the knots that are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the gnats have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then place in the nose a plug of cotton for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the tube is led in this way; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and it has a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the tip of the nose and grows rapidly until it becomes quite noticeable; for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of it, then apply a cautery or burning medicine to the area; if you delay cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of a reddish color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess, because when one cuts it sometimes great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a reddish color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then let the pus drain and cut without fear, and treat the area with drying and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of continuation come in one of these cartilaginous works, it benefits little, for in some men.
