Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then when this happens to anyone, if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips with a seam, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must then peel all parts of their skin until they heal, then bring together the two lips with a seam, and tighten them, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and ground incense over them; and place a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, there appears inside the lips an abscess hard, resembling grains of wheat, and smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut on each node, and take them with forceps and cut in each part; then apply the area after the incision of ground vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then wash it with oil, and treat the area with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times grows on the gums flesh attached, that the ancients call "albulus"; so you must hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and let flow the blood or the pus; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other powders restraining and drying; and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize it: it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the impurities
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, shells that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, such that the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are stinky; so you must make sit the patient between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or the shells appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are clean; and if what is there is removed at the first scraping, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one scrapes the teeth are different from those with which one scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth for its pain, you should delay extracting it as long as possible, for one must not do so; for it is a part of such high value that there is no justification for scraping it away.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract, you must be certain of the painful tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and have a good tooth extracted; yet the pain does not leave because of this, until the bad one is removed, as we have seen happen to these wise men; and when you are certain of the painful tooth, you must cut around the tooth entirely with a sharp instrument to protect the gums on all sides; then move it with your hands or with fine pliers little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the pliers; and have the patient's head in your lap between your knees, and hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push inside on each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, then you must fill it with cloths where the holes are; and then extract it carefully with tongs so that it does not break during extraction; and you must work very wisely around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well wary that you do not break it and leave a part behind, which may return to the patient through the mischief of the root causing greater pains than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act as the ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and recklessness sometimes break the tooth, and do not administer what we have recounted; but sometimes cause great illness through the opening for the roots that remain or for the tooth they break, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is drawn, wash the area with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply the area with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be toothed to hold the teeth firmly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the spot cotton moistened in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then use the forceps called "algefri," which resembles a chicken's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out entirely with tongs, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and put in the instrument which is called “althali”, that is to say a lever, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by this means, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which the form is here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools which are mentioned earlier in the discussion of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which the form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also of other instruments which are not counted; and the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the diseases show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of men; and if one breaks a cartilage or another bone where it could, then seek the instruments that are necessary, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to keep the bone so that it does not escape but can hold and remove it; then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, then clean it all with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body and its form is ugly, especially in unmarried women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after the tooth and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground: then you rasp it; and if it grows with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here shown, which resembles a small beak, and let it be of iron and sharp at the top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cutting little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file like the one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then flatten it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, you must file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth loosen, either by impact or by falling, and the patient cannot chew food without them falling out, and you have treated them with binding medicines but it does not work; then they must be bound with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes color; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and insert it doubled between two healthy teeth, then place the gaps between the loose teeth, whether one or more, until you reach wisely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the wrapping again from where you started, and draw your hand subtly and wisely so that nothing moves; and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the shoulder of the thread with pliers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread; it will remain and serve this way for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two false ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is reset in its place fresh and fresh, as we have said; and no one should intervene who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes they make the shape of a tooth from cow's bone, and put it where there is a deficiency, and tighten it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament that comes under the tongue is natural, which one is born with; or due to an accident from a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely so that the tongue is disengaged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, which is from a healed wound, put in the uncinus and cut widely this ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep for the artery below; and when you have done, wash the area with rose water and salt, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and the patient should change it every night so that the area cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put ground vitriol on the place; and if the blood persists, cauterize it with a lentigo-cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a pus color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it declines toward blenchore, and there is moisture, throw on it an ointment, cut it with a subtle spatula, and release it from one side to another; and if the blood persists in your work, put ground vitriol on until it is stopped, then return to your work until you extract all pus; then lift the place away from ash and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come into the throat swellings which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and of flesh color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but leave it until it turns black, and then you will divide it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of a white color tending, and the root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cut, but first check if the hot abscess rests and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his shoulders be in your hand, and work the mouth and take hold of the tongue with your hands, and press the tongue below all the instrument, which is its form; and it should be of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and stick it in the almond, and pull upwards as much as you can; and draw something from the cloth with it, then cut it with the instrument, which is its form, that looks like a forceps; and still the head is curved, and one end towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water mixed with salt, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate peel or myrtle leaves are boiled, or similar things, until the blood is stopped; then clean it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two almonds appear in the throat, so cut them in the same way as the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess born within her throat, that is to say, an abscess of the little sense; and it had almost completely closed off her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she had remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had put forth two streams through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then quickly and inserted one oncin in one nostril, then I drew it out and brought forth a great portion of pus; then I did the same on the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the oncin into these abscesses, and cut off a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the woman's throat, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again immediately, filling the place that I had emptied until it became very large; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow; and I departed from those parts, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the grape, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the hot abscesses are calmed, and they are fine, then you should cut it; and those that are round and compact and are not long; and they are bloody or of tawny color or black, then you should avoid incision on them.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then when you see it according to the method that I have said, of its blennorrhea and its length, you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the grape, and drag it below, and cut at T with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut beyond the excess which is outside the natural limit; for if you cut more, you harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use ingenuity in the cautery of his fearful sense.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then you press his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and mix with hot strong water so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this instrument, of which here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should have on the head a hair where one puts the medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that saliva and mucus run out of his mouth from the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and harm it; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for about half an hour, until you see it turned black and the bites of the medicine are calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton burns on the eye; do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, then restart it, and afterwards cautery around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around from the medicine; and let it be washed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more skillful than the incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamus and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put oil, and make boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot have the instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or brass, and let one of the pipes be put in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the ear through the tube, until the ear is mortified; afterwards, repeat this often, until the ear dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the hot abscess's onset, for many things may happen; and do not do this except when the hot abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put inside the head an eggshell so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to burden the mouth, and it is a good treatment altogether beneficial.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or spine of fish, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you should pull out what you can see and press the tongue with the tool under the sun so that you can see the thing move; and for what is not visible and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the stuck thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then make them swallow it; when it reaches the place, it will catch on, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take the fishing instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglote, that it does not come off, nor push the bone inside; and move such that the patient puts the instrument in, for which it is moved where the thing is pierced; so put it down or draw it out forcefully with all the instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the mucus is treated, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after which you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, then draw it out entirely with a small hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a horsehair cord, and insert it into the patient's throat, then heat the end of the horsehair cord, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient sweats with water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water, and work it in the mouth, and throw it inside without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the sinew feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then sub-fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned for the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and the pot is covered with a perforated cover, and in that hole be the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation in it, and the patient puts the end of the pipe in his mouth, and closes the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes to the phlegm; and the phlegm will now fall out, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient should suffer thirst, and eat salty and dry things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one extracts phlegm is, when it can be seen, similar to curved tongs for easy entry into the throat; and it resembles a bird’s beak, and has roughness like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot release; and you see here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what the memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own appearance, and from what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is different from that of the fundament, and the abscess of the fleshly part is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such that must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it swells around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For when the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay the puncture until it becomes dead, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the fundament, then pierce it before it becomes dead; and it is not appropriate to pierce a hard abscess without proper digestion completed, except for that which is near the fundament, so that it does not swell fully, extend inward, and become fistula; and cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for puncturing an abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and departure from fever, and reduction of the pain and redness, and weakening and sharpening at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you place the puncture at the lowest point of the abscess, where it opens up; and let the puncture be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all similar places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is best that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed after complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before then, the body of the venom from it will be prolonged, and it is full of much filth; and perchance the lips and the depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you administer small punctures in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many incisions according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the area and cut; when it has become as soft as a cloth, and is limp, then you must act as for buboes: and there are those that are divided into three angles, and there are those which are cut like myrtle leaves, such as abscesses of the armpits; and there are those where you make a round incision, and other cuts and similar operations.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, like superficial abscesses, you must pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but only part of it; then plug up the abscess until the next day, then draw some more; do this several times gradually, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is of weak strength, or pregnant women, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the sneezing sometimes occurs with the discharge of pus, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be aware of it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, clean the wound, and check if the abscess opening is small; and if it is a flat sore, apply lint or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many perforations, you must insert a wick into each so that they come one against the other; and if you have cut away part of the skin in the abscess and have shaven around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen scrap without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold and light water and wet the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then bring treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in their places in this book, and if it is winter time, and the area where the abscess is very nervous, you must place tents and cloths wet in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, you must place cloths wet in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then open the abscess and wipe and treat it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of the pouches
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, they are like fibers that are in webs, just like the down of a chicken, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and of such kind that they have moisture like veins; and there are those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you test with all the instrument which is called "intromissory," from which the forms come after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open on top of the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then peel without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will cure what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing of the night remains; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a fatty lump, then cut it according to this form, from its length; and sprinkle your powders, and scrape it on all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the cloth where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the stony and moist abscess, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and of those I cut an abscess on the head of an old woman; and found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck it, they would have made as much injury as to a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, whether those that come to the top of children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place, for pus to flow out; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often this abscess occurs on the neck, and under the jawbones, and in the glands, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are large, and they cluster together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its capsule, like a knot and an abscess on the head, as we have said; and the varieties of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are such ones that contain moisture, and there are harmful ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see of good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the flesh, and moves on all sides and is not swelled near the nerves of the neck nor at the artery nor at the conduit, and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut above it, and peel from each part, and extend the two lips of the wound with hooks if you need them, just as we have said in abscesses on the head; and pull out bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and let not the spatula be sharp or cutting, so the hand does not slip, and do not go too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to work, put in the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound tight; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softened, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you complete it; then seek out any remaining small swellings, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the swelling, you should not cut the swelling at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut away the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	and you must pay attention to cut the root of it, and pull hard, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold excess, pierce them where it appears to worsen; and pierce them thus as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, treat it with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of sprain
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke of the shaping of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have a sprain, it is necessary that the fold of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cleared; and if no help comes from this, because all the veins and the phlegm of the patient are inflamed in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the phlegm, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three circles or four with a small crosswise cut between the two circles or by the quantity of the superficial cut, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he must stretch the skin of the throat to the whole inch, then split the heart until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe that comes out through the place which is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one suspects strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and stitch all alone without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is entirely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the defect becomes apparent.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one cuts the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch the wound and cleanse it, until it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the uvula; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I knew that she had not cut a vein or artery but only the throat, and air was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young lady except that her voice became hoarse, and she later returned to normal; for this reason, I say that there should be no fear in sewing the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess of the color of jaundice, and it occurs mostly in women; and it comes in two ways: natural, and accidental; the natural one has no sign.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one comes in two ways, of which one resembles fatty knots, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from arterial knots; and there is fear, and it does not befit to work with fire except in the small ones, and examine and search throughout the insertion: if you find it like a fatty knot, and it cannot enter any vein, cut it as one cuts the knots, and pull out all its hood if there is any; and thoroughly investigate well, and treat it as appropriate until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods from us exist, of which I will speak all the likenesses; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference that is between knot and discharge.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is heat and fever lasting until the boiling has passed, and putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the knot, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains its own sac, which is according to the color of the body, and begins like a cyst, and becomes large; and there are according to two likenesses, either dry or moist, and much in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the wound, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "introducer", according to what its form will come in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of investigating abscesses of the nose is that you take the wettest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the introducer, and be careful in this so as not to use too much force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running liquid comes out, whatever color it has, cut it open as I have said for other abscesses; and if no moisture comes after the introducer, know that it is fatty, so then cut it in a cross shape, take it with forceps, and scrape it lightly on each side and watch the coat where it lies so you can draw it out clean with the wound; and if you cannot draw it out clean, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the pus returns many times; and if a little remains and causes you pain, use some corrosive powders on the wound, bind the wound, and put things that soothe a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pus is large, sew the two lips of the wound together, and treat it with what promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pulsating vein is against you or other such that it hastens, use the place of ground vitriol and leave it light for two days or three, until the wound rots, and stops the boiling of the blood; then return copper to what remains of the pus.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the penetrating instruments, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret," and one called "breb," and they come in three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they are like needles used for sewing sores, and they are made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and black lead is more tested for encircling the ulcerations of fistulas; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the tweezers are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are tweezers that have two curves in three ways also; and there are tweezers that have three curves, and they too are in three ways; and there are tweezers that have two curves, and tweezers with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these which are used for cutting is sharp, and there are some that do not cut from one side so they can peel the skin without cutting the vein or nerve; and among these introductive tools are the lancets placed in sheaths, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are only used in fleshy areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes another instrument is made small, resembling onion skins, according to this form, with which blood is staunched.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed sometimes at the site that heals with cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them must thread according to this form from line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then peel the fat, and apply a medicine to heal flesh on the wound, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast sags down and is softened due to its size as it happens with women, cut it in two parts above, by two similar slits; so that one adheres to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then peel the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula with edges, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, apply the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the kind of scrofula, then cut it as we have said for incisions of scrofula, and if the wound emits pus, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above is sealed, often abscesses occur; and similarly happens to the swollen vein and abscess; and thus it is known when it is for the artery, then the abscess is long in appearance; and when you feel it with your hands, you sense the constriction; and when it is for the vein, then it appears less firm underneath; and it is folly to cut this abscess, especially when it is under bones and joints and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very dangerous.
