Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid surgical treatment with iron, and the one at the head should also be avoided; in those swollen by artery, make an incision above the skin of the length; then work the incision into small pieces, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath and pierce through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a double thread at two points according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples; then puncture the area between the two ties with an introductor until the blood comes out which is there, and free the abscess; then treat as if it were a boil, until the threads fall off; then cure with ointment suitable for this, until it heals; and if the abscess is the size of the vein, you should hold in your hand all that you can reach from the abscess to the skin, then place a needle underneath where you are holding in your hand, and pierce through, and tie off with a double thread so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have said, or tie one of the two parts at both ends of the thread; and if you fear that the threads will not stay, place another needle underneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie off in four places; then cut open the abscess until the excess comes out, then remove the excess from the heart and leave what is tied; then place a cloth moistened with wine and oil on top, then treat it with dressings and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, so do abscesses come to the nerves when they are wounded, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hands and all places where there are joints, and it is grievous abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it exists in many positions without pain; and when it is pressed firmly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all sides, neither forward nor backward, nor below nor above, and those that are in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps contraction would result; and those that are on the head or forehead, slice the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with some tweezers, and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with an awl, then scrape it, remove it, and stitch up the wound, curing it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the abdomen and not elsewhere, which is a disease called "fungus" by resemblance to them, and its roots are subtle, and the growths are large; there are small ones and very large ones; I saw a person who had two in their abdomen that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had fine roots, were deeply split, and immediately oozed moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six and a half, and in the work of the incision you must observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist and of subtle root; then cut it with a wide spatula, and have the fire cautery at hand.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting comes often too great a flow of blood, and if the blood overcomes you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision with the iron, take a properly made thread of linen, and tie it on the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then bind it again, and do not stop binding the linen thread until you cut the joint, and it falls off by itself without effort; and if the roots are large, there is fear in cutting especially for the abdomen, but you can well cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not grow back; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the skin which is of red color and poor feeling and looks pale.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess infected, and I will come to the treatment of the sore afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil is about to burst.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a tear in the skin, and it is on the belly and some of the boils occur as they happen in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to the rupture of the skin and the discharge of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light matter without pain, and it discharges in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestines, then it is more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers, it sinks in and then returns, and sometimes it becomes hard, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and from strenuous labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess opens with these signs: large and hard, planted according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to arterial blood, or veinous blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	And it is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear with it, as I have said in the chapter about abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to intestine or pus, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to lie on his back, and be stretched out straight, then apply a cloth all around the swelling; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area you have wrapped with the entire spatula, then extend half of the abscess above with the large uncine; then bind it around with a strong thread or cord made of thick silk firmly, and let the knot from the binding be loose; then work on the extended part of the abscess over the binding, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, untie it, and push the intestine upward out of the belly; and if you find pus, take it with the uncine, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go around gently, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and stick the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you pierce; then draw out the abscess at four points over the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the area until it rots, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or cut it when it becomes fine and rotten, then cure it as necessary, and clear the abscess as we have said; then extract any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as necessary, and sew up the area.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid the iron cure; and we say the ulcer in the armpit requires great caution in its treatment, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in a place where they can be scraped off like ulcers which are on the breasts, and in the thigh, and in similar places, and it must be completely removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I have never been able to heal any; no one has ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then make him sweat if there is evident fullness, then prepare the patient's body well to perform the work; then apply your knives to the ulcer, and scrape all around, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press the area with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding stops you from making an incision in the artery or vein, then cauterize until the blood is stilled; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division the types of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each type, and the treatment done by medicines, and that which is treated by iron: it is only edema; and one should not touch iron on these two types: known as tympanites and hyposarche, for it is a deadly thing; then when you treat this type of dropsy called "edema" with medicines, and the treatment does not work, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as fever and dysentery and similar things; do not touch iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but only dropsy, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient straight up on your hands, and the assistants press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the body, then take the spathulum with thorns according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the tip, and all the while it should not be so penetrating that it can reach the intestine when you insert it, nor can it injure; then look if the dropsy is inclined towards the intestines: then you must cut three times directly below on the side of the pulse; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be to the left of the vein three times; and if it is for the spleen, then to the right, and it should not be that the patient lies on the incision so that the excesses do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, insert it, and lift your hand with all the spatula between the skin and the surface as if removing a layer about the size of a fingernail or around it; then pierce the surface until the fluid comes to an empty space, which is where the water lies, then draw it out forcefully, and insert this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver wire, and it is made of brass or light iron, and at the lower part there is a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two from another side, and one from another; and the head is shaped like a quill, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it should now rise with the instrument; empty then half or a third part, for if you empty more than necessary at this time, perhaps the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the treatment, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their pulse; then pull out the instrument and retain the water, which is retained now for the plug that stops the hole on top of the syphon, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument another day if you see the patient enduring this, and draw a small quantity of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to follow until there remains but a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave much water in him, cure it with burial or hot sand, and by sweating a lot or bathing and in the sun, and dye from drinking; and treat it with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	about the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to pierce it immediately with a very fine instrument throughout according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put in the opening a fine plug of lint, and bind it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug, let him urinate, then replace it; and perhaps none is needed, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small is treated with the plug of lint, as we have said, so it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are defective, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot straddle because the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, then extends the head of the rod and cuts it as the length of a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should be; and beware of blood flow which comes often, and if it happens, then stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathe comes on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle lancet, cut and clean them all, then put moist cotton with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of putrid color and stinking, then you must apply cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the abscess is at the tip of the penis, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the abscess that is inside first; and when it is sealed, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, the head of the penis is not secure and may be pierced, leading to blackening and corruption in the penis and testicles; then you must remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and beans, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two dispositions together: that is to say, with bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you should insert a tube of bronze into the urethra of the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the foreskin is dry at the end of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or where there is an injury or abscess, then you must peel it with an instrument carefully, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides; and if it is difficult to separate this, then you should peel it with a spatula slightly from the tip of the penis and the skin; then gently separate them, and place a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water between them, so that it does not dry out again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a loosening of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our own will, and particularly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, for it is not used in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions around Idal, and with forceps, and with a new scalpel; the blood would flee because there are two layers, and perhaps one cuts the upper layer and leaves the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is cut short, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleaning from the nail there is not assurance of the tip of the member; and in the cleaning of the nail perhaps the iron slips, and ruins the work, and often they are born thus that they do not need cleaning and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with force on all the thread of the ligament I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts exactly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, you cut equally all the time; but let the thread be tight around the skin; and let the method of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis just so, then give him hope in every way you can; then have him stand between your hands straight, and hide the forceps between your hands or under your feet so the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow on the urethra, and pull it up until the head of the penis is in; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the tip with a double thread, then tie below the pouch to another ligature; hold it with two fingers by the second ligature at the pouch and thumb, and cut between the two ligatures, then lift the heart up quickly and pull the head of the penis; then let the blood flow little by little, for this is the best; and put powder on top of the powder one cloth glued with a yolk of an egg cooked mixed with rose water, cooked with good fresh oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it again as needed until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for purification is this: the two shoulders should be held and should be sharp, and the shoulders should also be as large as the sleeve evenly:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification is when the pus inside flows at the incision; then you must extend it with your nail, unless the skin forms an abscess; and cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it lasts more than three days, and what is beneath the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is warm and calm, and scrape it lightly; cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the penis, for it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the area of things that are hot with powder, which we have said in the treatise on powders, and if one cuts from the heart beyond measure, and it goes above, it will not harm; treat it then as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by the obstruction of stones, or congealed blood, or feces, or foreign matter, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone located at the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over his knees; and their feet should be placed on their back, extending their belly upwards towards the back, and restrain the patient as tightly as they can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expulsion of the stone above, which releases the urine; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which this is the form: and it should be made of fine and light silver, like bird feathers; and its length should be one and a half palms, and it should be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is that you take a double thread, and tie at the head a ball of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the catheter; and cut the excess wool and put it up to the head of the catheter, then anoint the catheter with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a chair, and wash the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the catheter into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the catheter forward up to the bladder, and the patient feels it reach the empty space, and this is not done according to this order forcefully because the tube or where it goes is twisted; then stretch the thread with all the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull out forcefully, and make flow the urine; and repeat the catheterization until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood comes into the bladder, or corruption is gathered there, and you see aqueous and medicinal substances being distilled into it, then make use of all the instrument called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the end is made in such a way that the medicinal cord can plug the penis well without addition, so that one can draw moisture from it and push when necessary; and when you want to inject your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the tube into the moisture, and pull with the plunger inside; thus you will draw the moisture into the syringe, and then reseal the plunger tightly; then the moisture will enter and come to the bladder now so that the patient can feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysterizes the bladder: here it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and below at the groin where the ligaments fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you want to use for the enema into the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts properly with a strong double thread, and heat that moisture over fire; then place the head of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder so all the moisture comes out gradually until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle from it, and pierce it roundly around; then put a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a lid, and place inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, press by hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	about the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone attached to the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone attached to the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and it is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder resembling subtle urine; and there appears sand, and it irritates the patient's penis, and it can happen many times, and then stiffens; and much of this jumping affects the foundations; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and it is very severe in elders, and it is moderate for young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with a cathartic, to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and raise him up and move him downward so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it leaves its higher position; then make him sit between your hands placed together, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then seek it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the full touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is an adult, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown youth; and insert it into his anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then lean it towards the neck of the bladder; then press down on your finger, and push it outward where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instructs the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and commands him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part where one makes the incision; then he inserts the sharp spatula, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but to the side of the left thigh; and let it be straight towards the stone, and your hands should be near the anus, and let the cut be transverse so that it is wide at the surface, and inside narrow according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the hand at the anus will cause it to jump out without effort; and know that there are such stones with angles and edges: these are difficult to remove; and there are those that are smooth, resembling a grain, and round, from which the extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margins, make the size larger; and if it does not jump out, then you must grasp with tweezers that are like a file at the tip, to tightly grasp the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below the instrument subtle curved at the tip; and if you cannot eject it thus, then enlarge the bladder opening, and if the sinews peel off, then tighten with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, then place first the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut up, then draw out forcefully, and the small ones after if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you must saw it and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out where the wound cannot heal; but nevertheless exert yourself in drawing it out, or breaking it with tweezers, until you pull it out piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, then apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tightly, and place on top a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lay the patient back on his side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, wash the area very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment diaphoretic and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and corroding come to the wound and clots of blood in the bladder, which cause urine retention, conceived in such a way that it does not pass with the urine: then put your finger into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and destroy it; then cleanse the wound with water and ash and salt, and aid it in all ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour when you treat it, you bind both thighs together, and apply medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the duct of the penis, fixed inside, and the urine cannot pass; then treat it as I said before, that you cut it many times, so one is spared from the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron bar according to this form and let it have three pointed ends fixed in one piece.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the bar into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the bar in your hand against the stone little by little, until you can pierce through the other side of the stone; then urine will flow soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is broken immediately, and it comes out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie a thread under the stone and another above, then cut the penis where the stone is between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is formed in women, and if it ever does happen, the treatment is difficult, and it is prevented for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will expose herself to midwives, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deep perfected than the stone of the man, therefore it must make a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if necessity calls for this, then you must take a midwife well knowledgeable, and hardly one is found, and if you do not find one, then seek out a subtle male doctor; and present to him a wise bailiff in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her that she perform what you command for the inquiry of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it must put his finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her hand, and recommend to her that she put her finger in the con of the patient, and seek and press her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then she must move it from the entrance of the bladder downwards to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is arranged to be moved, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision at first be small; then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone increase the wound until the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many kinds of stones: to be known, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and know the similarities to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the pain overcomes you, then apply ground vitriol to the place for an hour until the pain subsides; then return to your work until the stone comes out, and have the instruments I have told you about for extracting the stone from men to help you in your work; and if the pain overcomes you, and it is from the artery that is cut, then apply the powder to the place and use bandages tightly, and do not start this again, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, lest the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limb becomes strong, return to your work, until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquous ramice is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is beneath the heart of the testicles, containing the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one might think it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is due to the weakness that comes to the testicles, and that material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion upon the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: whether it is color declining to jaundice, or without red, or black, or white watery, and this happens more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is in the white as we have said, then the abscesses are hard, a little long like the figure of an egg, and the testicles do not appear, for they are moist all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the inner membrane, then the abscesses are hard with a part of the egg, and for this reason, one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white surface, then it can be felt well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, then test throughout the entire inserted area, from which the form is as mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient should be well anointed according to our ability and the plenitude of his body; then he lies on his back, on something slightly raised, and put many cloths underneath him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the testicles' core; then take the sharp spatumile, and cut the skin of the testicles in half from long down to near the base, and let that cut be straight, dividing the testicles' skin all the way to the white surface, and scrape it delicately according to our ability; then pierce the white part full of fluid with a wide hole, and drain all the fluid, then place your probes, and stretch the white part upwards; do not touch the core of the testicles, but only that white part; cut everything carefully in pieces, especially the side of it delicately, for if you do not cut it well, the fluid will return; and if the egg jumps due to your work, then reset it to its place when you have completed the work on the white part; then join the two sides of the testicles' core with a stitch, then treat as other wounds until they are healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you tie up the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the flow of blood; then cut off the testicle at all its suspensory parts, and extract the egg, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the fluid is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut off the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe off the blood, and put in the wound wool soaked in rose oil; and place beneath it more wool soaked in wine and oil, and put over both testicles, and cover with doubled cloths, and tie it up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool according to this likeness and let them be sewn together at the waistband of the breeches, and one side of the shoulder should extend from the fundament up to the back, and the other to the part of the groin; and the other two ends over the two angles, and let all the binding come together in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of an iron shears, and that you take a subtle knife-shaped cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing the fluid is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that surface with the points, and scrape it with this hot subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all manners that you can, until you make everything clear; and be careful that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and pay attention to prevent blood flow, and do it more than the other works of cutting; and if anything opposes you, whether a hot abscess or blood flow or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this work due to its horror, then administer puncture as I tell you, and know that when you are certain by the signs we have said that aqueous matter is present, situate the patient on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess below at all parts of the broad spatiumile, and place the puncture deep into the body; let the holes be wide so that all the water flows out freely; then put cotton on the spot and bind it, leaving to drain the remaining water; then treat until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow from the mouth of the wound, you must insert a quill or an instrument used to draw water from dropsical patients, whose form was described earlier; enlarge the opening of the wound, knowing that the water returns and accumulates after about six months or thereabouts, and when it is gathered as before, thus will the patient pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many positions, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and the similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and especially to the testicles; and this is by a great chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by excess of sour and watery substances, which spread to the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a severe abscess; and by chance some severe abscesses are fearful and stony, and of a flaming color, and sometimes comes from an artery knot, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by artery, it is known by the position of hot abscess when you press it with your hands; and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is affected by vein swelling is known by its appearance upon touching with the hands, and one can easily perform surgery on this condition, and on other similar cases; and it is that you cut the core of the testicles, then the egg rises up, and the thread from the white part comes out, and release the suspensory ligament from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already swollen with these new conditions, then you must draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is airy on the surface or in what is inside the vessels, you must release all of that tension and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the rear place, then you must cut it all off and extract the egg, just as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are completed, then apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in a covering similar to a boil, with the swelling of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when urinating; and the treatment of this disease is just as fearful as the previous one, yet we will still tell you the procedure for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the scrotum down to your hands, to all the vessels that are close to the penis, and hold the main ones, and stretch them well; then cut with a broad sharp spatumile across the middle of the vessels until they are exposed, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then fix a needle with double thread, and tie it at the first place where the pus comes out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as the others where you anoint oil, so that no vessels fall that nourish one of the testicles; because by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels produce pus, it is necessary to drain all the vessels from the testicles; so that the seed does not lose its nourishment due to the cutting of the vessels, dry up and cannot help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this condition are due to the rupture that comes from the spleen, or the extension on the belly in the area of the ribs, causing the intestines to descend into one of the testicles; and this rupture is either from the spleen itself, or from its extension, and these two types come from causes such as impact, jumping, falling, lifting heavy loads, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the spleen are that they happen little by little over a long time, not suddenly; and the swellings are equal up to their peak because the spleen presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is from the rupture of the spleen, that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the swellings appear varied under the skin nearby, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestines and the body beyond the spleen.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the hernias come with the intestines, and are held there, causing great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, therefore one must avoid them.

And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to hold the intestines with his hand inside the wound if he can enter; then be mindful on his neck between your hands, and lift the thighs; then stretch the heart above, and cut all the skin of the scrotum down long; de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia

Sometimes rupture occurs in the arteries, as we have said, and the opening appears; and none of the intestines descend to the groin, and if any do descend, it is rare, and repairs itself often; and yet if it remains too long at this point, the wound grows or the scrotum swells until the intestines descend; and this happens due to the extension of the scrotum which is in the arteries, as we have said, because it extends, then softens and swells the opening and appears; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and that the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen part of the rupture according to the width of three fingers; and then draw out the scrotum which is under the skin following, then take the rod and place it over the exposed area of the scrotum; and press it tightly against the belly, then sew the two exposed areas of the scrotum on top of the head of the rod, and sew one and the other; then draw out the head of the rod, and do not cut into the scrotum nor extend the eye or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the separation of the intestines; then heal it by the treatment of wounds.
