de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often, the skin of the testicles softens in some men because the substances inside are softened, and it is clear to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, that the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a suture, and if you want, sew first the excess of the softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the sutures, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	from the chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that chastisements are disapproved in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one is that doctors should know how to respond when asked, and understand the treatment; and the other, because we often need the chastisement of certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castrations are done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging down; then take them in your hand, pulling until they are dislocated and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For the castration of the animal: you must paint the beast, and press its testicle skin with your left hand, then tie up the suspensory, and cut on each egg once, when you have properly flayed them; and leave some fat of the surface and the thin layer of fat that is on the vessels; this method of castration is more severe than that done by attraction because in the attraction sometimes something of the testicles remains, which makes the beast desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	about hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways in humans: one is when between the two testicles there appears something like the formation of a woman's anatomy, where it has hair, and sometimes it urinates through it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, and it is on the wrist like a rod and two eggs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you cut all the attached parts, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a part attached to the natural area, so that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come there; or it is caused by a thin or thick surface, and formed perfectly in the middle, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes the menstrual flow; and knowledge of this is by examination.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is closely appearing, then grasp it with your hands or with a cloth.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of the subtle surface and it is close to the two lips, then hurry, and do it thus: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then stretch the two lips properly until the subtle surface becomes round and covers the swelling; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and have the woman lie with a man each day so that it may not become dry.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the surface is hard and thick, then you should scrape it with a spatula shaped like a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez. Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when new flesh comes in the wound, it must be cut according to this method, unless they are infected abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess that is in the wound, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood usually flows without clotting, and when hemorrhoids are old they become withered; and we have said before in the division their similarities, and the signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that the hemorrhoids and the withered parts, when they are perfect in the anus, and they do not appear to the touch, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold room, then stretch the hemorrhoid with tongs and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders that stop bleeding, such as gallnut and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then raise her legs against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a poultice to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is stopped, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if not, have leeches applied to the back and breasts without pricking; then take wool, and moisten it in plantain juice or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut as I have said for the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the jaw
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the jaw, such as ulcers and stony abscesses and herpes and aphthae and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is then necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes on the jaw, which is not one of those abscesses that are picked by a bowe; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and whether it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it fester until the pain is calmed; and then sit the patient on a chair, and have two small stools where he leans, and support his back and bring his feet together behind the leg; and let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good binding; then turn the bail to the right side, and apply the instrument used for the mouth of the jaw, from which comes the form; and it is necessary that when you apply this instrument, you first fix the point to know the depth of the jaw, so that what enters does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the jaw with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause distress; and it is necessary that he place the tip of the instrument on top, and paint the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and one cuts it with a soft hand, then it must be cut at the head, to the white spatumile; and when the bowel is emptied, then you must put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in dried green oil; and place the tent far from the wound into the flesh pulp, and put on top of the pulp and on the finger clean wool moistened in water or malves boiled; then cure it after two days of ointment application like this, until it is healed; and sometimes one lifts the flesh pulp and the wound by aclyster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and long aristology boiled; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is embedded in the flesh, then you must beware of using hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife to know the signs of natural childbirth, which are when you see the woman leaning down and wanting to smell the air: then the child hurries to come out forcefully; then you know that this childbirth follows the natural course, with the head coming out first, followed by the afterbirth; and when you see these signs, you should gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it rises up its head, the afterbirth follows it, and the mother is cleansed of her superfluities through proper cleansing; and he who comes in another way does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out on its feet, and the body or the shoulders or the hands come out first, or it comes out belly-first or breech-first, and is turned by chance onto its neck, and in other harmful positions; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, wary of error and deception, and I will show you all the positions and how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes onto its head through natural passage, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle where women hold her; and boil her natural substance in oil or fenugreek, and then the midwife puts between her fingers the small spatula of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the amnion, and scrape until the moisture inside flows out; and hold the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then enema the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil; then make her sneeze and snort from condyse, and keep her mouth and nose covered for an hour: now the infant will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out weak, then you must reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot go in, then put the woman on one chair, and lift her feet up high; then stand the chair on the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when setting it down; and if the hand cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that was placed here before, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, then you must push it up; and then turn it little by little until it is aligned; then take one of the feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, then order it to be grasped and make it sneeze with condiments; if it is strong, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not become strong as we have said, then turn it little by little until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come strong as we have said, then take muslin of altitude, and sesame oil, and dissolved gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside to strengthen this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to the ribs; and when she is softened below, make her wear a necklace of myrrh, and place it underneath, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently grasp her belly, for the child will jump now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife gently places her hands on it; then she tilts it back by its neck, and lets its feet hang down, and has it lying on the bed; and she gradually bends its hands, and then takes hold of its hands over the belly, and removes the cushions underneath, until it is aligned downward; and if the child does not jump out, she takes its feet and forcefully moves them, then pushes the belly upwards, then puts her hands in; and gently pulls the child out; and commands the woman to strain so that the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child who comes with one hand extended wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on the bed, and stretch out her legs properly; then administer the medicine I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, and attempt to bring back the hand; and deliver the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to pull so that the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its neck, and have its hands spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the midwife holds her hand, then turns it little by little, and delivers it gently; and when it is aligned, apply the natural medicine of altitude and oil, as we have said, then command her to move little by little; and once you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to pull; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this manner to all the secondine, cut the secondine with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the infant can lift its face and neck, then cut it from the bud so that it is not held back, and kill the infant; then put the child inside again until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to grab hold of herself: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things and do not live, if any name; I know these that they are multiplied, and are severed by the tool that divides them, which is tied to the flesh; and sometimes they come out as naturally as some eggs, just as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out painfully, then treat them as we have said, and let the bandage be fine, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as it is worth moving towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or many up to fifteen, and they are fully formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and it is necessary that the bandage know all this, for perhaps similar things happen; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound strength, and has no accident where she fears death; then it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the helper holds her in two parts, where she is tied to the bed so that she is not moved during the descent of the child; then anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of alum and fenugreek and linseed, then anoint both sides of her hands with these oils and these mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb, then search for the place where she places the hooks that are suitable for this purpose, and be careful if the child is positioned so that it descends on its head; then insert the hooks in its eyes or in its neck or in its mouth or in its palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the sides, and if the descent is at feet, then place them in the ankles and the middle ribs; and it is necessary that he holds the hook with his right hand, and places the forceps between his fingers of the left hand, and gently insert it all her hand, and insert the hook into one of these places we have said until it reaches the empty space; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then place against the other tooth, or a third if necessary, so that the extraction is even; and then extend evenly by moving from one side to the other, for them to come out, and let the teeth be notched to hold them, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then anoint the soft parts of his fingers with oil, and place them in that part, and pull the other part; and if any point remains, then put this tooth or higher part, and do this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other and cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it comes out completely; then cut it at the joint of the palm or thumb, and thus you should do the same for the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow at the exit, or it has a pointed top gathered together, then you must put the spiked spatula between your fingers, cut the top and extract the point; or grind it with the tool which is called «almidach», from which the form comes with the tools in the chapter that follows this one; and do the same if the child naturally has a large head; and then pull out the bones with the tongs, and if the head jumps out forcefully and holds onto the forceps, let it be split so that the moisture which is in the pus can exit; and if it cannot exit, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it swells in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, then the attraction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the wound is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the belly or the breast, then you must stretch it with the cloth wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or the breast until the moisture inside flows out; and if other limbs are removed and the head remains, then the healer places his hand at the depth of the wound and pulls it to the mouth of the wound; then insert one ounce or two, and pull strongly; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, do not work on it, but apply moist and fatty things; and apply plasters, and sitz baths in softening and moistening waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on its side, and you can make it straight, then apply what we have said for the living child; and if one cannot do so, then pull it out by parts, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for hot abscesses that come in the marrow; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with binding water, and other treatments should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb one fetus had been dead, then another was placed on top of it, and the other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came upon the boil, and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to have great pus.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat, and I thought long about it, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strongly attracting poultice, and an bone came out, and after some days others did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound, and pulled out many bones, until the woman was much better; and the woman lived for a long time thereafter, and there was still a little pus coming from the place; and I have recalled this chapter not only because when masters find something strange, they should take note to record it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the dislocated to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, with which books are pressed; and it has two wheels at the two ends of the two shafts.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the restrictoire, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the handle should be one inch wide, and the margin of the sides one inch, and in length one and a half palms; and between the two shafts should be two adjustments of this same handle, which are fixed on one side and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the dislocated area to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of tongs; and let it have at both ends two attachments, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the womb with all the instrument, make the woman sit on one bed, feet hanging and legs spread, then insert the two attached parts together into the womb, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand at the entire instrument as you have done with the tongs evenly, according to the amount that you wish to open the mouth of the womb, until the servant does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all superior, and their forms are numerous; and when the physicians have them prepared, the work is much faster, and more prestigious for men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument that you have prepared, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold back her urine, and then make her sneeze with condii, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare, such as calamus, rue, anise, camomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled in water over the fire in the pot; then place one end of a cane in the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare, and blow until the vapors come into the mare; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The sinews move swiftly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not go away, instruct the nurse to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in muslin of alum, and then place it naturally, and seek the sinew; and when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straightly, so that the wound does not close during the extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come out and become untangled.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the wound is very narrow, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not come out completely as we have said, be careful not to force in pulling; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the wound, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then give her a clyster of an ointment tetra-pharmaceutical; she will expel and reset, and it will come out; however, when she expels, there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is then appropriate fumigations for this: some of the ancients have experienced the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the flows and the secondina is thus:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a cane, and one puts the fine end in the part, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and keep it going until it is spent, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have a pierced anus, but it is plugged with a thin membrane: so it is then the duty of the nurse to pierce that membrane appropriately, and not use a sharp spatula, and be careful not to touch the stitches; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, then continue the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, put a pin of silver in the puncture and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wishes to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this swelling comes from the adhesion of a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cut that adhesion: then it should be treated, as we have said about the pin of silver.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come below the anus are nodules and swellings that occur near the anus or in the space of two parts, and there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and often emits white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are perforated; they are identified by what comes out during defecation or flatulence when the patient defecates, and occasionally some come out suddenly.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that extend to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; they reach to the hip joint, and to the buttock of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula that penetrates to the anus and the one that does not penetrate: it is when you put your index finger in the anus, and insert a fine needle of glass or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, then insert a thin lead tent or a horsehair until you feel the tent or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of excrement, wind, or worm as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; do not hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends all the way to the bladder or to the urinary duct, then the urine leaks out and cannot be sealed with medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it extends to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling comes all the way to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the source of pain around it, then it immediately flows out, and neither medicine nor ointment helps; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the vanity of foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those that are not penetrating and not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs inclined towards his abdomen; then insert a probe of silver, or of bronze if there is tortuosity, until you know where the swelling comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must put your index finger in there, and if you then feel that the tentacle has pierced it; and whether uncovered or where you feel between your finger the surface or the flesh, then you know that it is perforated; do not work on it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can sometimes heal some cases, but it rarely happens; and the aid that one does is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was previously mentioned; and put it completely hot into the fistula until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times until you know that the foul flesh has been burned, which looks like a bird's feather; then clean it with cloths moistened in butter until that flesh comes out, then clean it with an ointment that heals and seals the flesh.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is done, he cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters, and does not pierce to the bone at its base, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick cover of flesh or sinew, and you see the fistula under this cover from the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push the tent forward immediately, and then cauterize afterward until you reach the head of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall out; then cleanse those foul flesh that resemble a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sinew overpowers you and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal heat.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire gathers two good things: to know, the burning of these wounds joined, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then clean the wet tents with butter or ground things, until the pus flows out, and leaves the burned wound in the pus; then treat the wound with heating ointments that soften hard flesh, and are the medicines dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the perfect part of the anus and is away from the body, put your finger in the anus and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between two is the thread or the sinus or wound, where it is close to piercing, there should be no force but way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut until the bottom, or if you can put tents and treat as first; and do not go too deep into perfection, that you do not cut the tissue holding the anus, and excretions come out without will; then treat it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it is cut near the anus, either by tent or by another pointed instrument; then cleanse that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and keep the fistula in the part outside the anus: this will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are according to this manner: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you put the twisted thread in two, and insert the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated on the edge of the fundament inside, then draw out the thread from that perforation, just as you insert your finger into the fundament; and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and bind them to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and sometimes tighten it until the thread cuts through the tissue that is between the two, and they fall out; then treat the wound until it is healed and closed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it pierced in every way you can, if it is not too hard.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to cut so hard for the lancing, and then clean it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile spike used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side not, so that one does not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are according to two manners: some are inside the anus, like resin grains, and they can be small or large, and they bleed a bit; and there are one or more of them, and they are outside the anus at its head; but those that are outside have little moisture, and also bleed a bit with some yellow water or a bit of blood, and they have the color of flesh. The cure for those who have them inside the anus is to instruct the patient to defecate in a chamber pot so that the anus protrudes, and the threads appear; then quickly grasp it with forceps, or hold it with your fingernail, cut it at its roots; and if the uncine cannot hold them due to moisture, take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of linen; pull them out with your hands, then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders that serve as cautery on top; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter about cautery, then treat it further until healed. If the anus cannot protrude, give the patient an enema with a harsh and biting solution to wash what is inside the anus so that it can clearly come out; when the patient sits down, if the threads are outside the anus, the cure is light; you take them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them, then treat as we have said until healed, and avoid cutting with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must administer the stitch according to this method: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so be wide; and pull the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to let out the excess blood; then put on the wound a moist cloth in rose oil or in ointment, and apply it to the wound, and instruct the patient that he should rest; and then leave them until they fall off, and when they have fallen off, treat with anointing and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the feces or wound
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often it happens that dryness of phlegm occurs in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must scrape at the point of a spit or with your nail the bark above, which does not let it moisten; then cleanse it until it is sodden as it should be; and if it cannot become sodden, then start shaving more forcefully than before, until it heals much, and is peeled; then clean it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from the trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small spotted appearance around the body, and it spreads very quickly; sometimes cold causes it, and it is felt like death from trembling, and it comes all over the body, more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and put that quill on the boil, so that the circle properly encircles the boil all around; then turn your hand all around the quill until you cut all around the boil, and place it perfectly, and remove the boil from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a quill of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be sharp below and broad above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, to hold the boil in place and press it. And if you wish, cauterize the boil as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	about the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or brass, or melted tin or lead; and sometimes these substances are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are administered in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster, whether small or large, is wide at the top, where the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the end should be pierced inside; and it should have two holes on one side, and one hole on the other; and the belly where one puts the medicines should be made of a beast's bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one inch of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread of raw silk through these holes ten or so times around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie the instrument in front with a strong thread, then perform the clyster; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then the minister spreads his two hands together until it is all closed, then remove the clyster, and lift the patient’s legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold it as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize in a disease of diarrhea, and the medicine rushes to come out, restart it until it is absorbed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus, or an abscess, then let the clyster be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine clyster on which the skin is constricted:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made by, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cutting of sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or that they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that lies on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the striking of stones or similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound large, and you fear slightly an abscess forming: then make it bleed freely from the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the wounded part; and purge the patient of excess wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not bleed freely, reduce his food intake, and let him drink no wine nor eat meat; and apply to the wound, if hot abscesses form, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder which I will mention a little later; and if the sun has moved it, then apply some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by bandages, then bring them together by suturing, as I will say about abdominal wounds, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can, and holds only by a little bit, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, as well as beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotting skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut out all the rot completely and throw it away, then treat the wound; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put in this powder which soothes as soon as the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is: take one part incense; dragon's blood two parts; live coals three parts, and powder them finely, and apply to the wound, and press it firmly, until it dries well and adheres to all its blood; then bandage it tightly, and leave it undisturbed, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with coals alone, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, especially in its state, one does not put this powder there; but puts on some digesting ointments, or poultice of barley flour made with water and honey, until it gives pus; then cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then I will extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other method than to leave the treatment and not apply anything restraining, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation with each other is connected to the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be below, such as hot washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumis also washed in sweet water, and other minerals according this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce it at the lowest point; and if an artery is cut and blood flows out continuously, open it up, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the thorn of the throat is cut or the passage, but the tube that carries the food remains intact, sew the passage back onto the canal of the throat, do not touch the throat itself but reset it according to its natural form; then bind it moderately, leave it for some days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has affected the bone, clean it out; and if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave them until the wound suppurates, and clear and relieve the discharge; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if air escapes when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it tightly because the blood does not coagulate properly and returns to the heart, killing the patient; but apply an attractive ointment and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and make the patient sleep on the side of the wound for three days, or four, or more; there will be no spasm, nor trembling, nor constriction when breathing; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
