Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and acts up, know then that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, on the thigh or the back, treat it with what is in front; if it is large, by suturing; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and pieces have been chopped off, then clear the wound, and pull out the nails if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound rot, which will lighten the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgement is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines jump out, causing internal penetration; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the smaller wound is worse than the larger one, because one does not reset the intestines properly when they are not placed hot to hot; for the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, making it harder to reset them, and thus the medium-sized wound is better because one can repeatedly place the intestine in its proper position more often. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: two common sutures occur at the suture of the belly, and the other wounds of the body have two other specific sutures; yet they are still more specific to the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put back, this is due to one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: soak a sponge or some cloth in warm water only, or you boil in water squinant and cypress and spike, and wet the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this makes the wine constricting, and it is better to do so alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water in which althea and mallows have been boiled, for by this the entrance is made easier; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be to cut rather than the slicing, which one should not do without great necessity; and this is the instrument for making the incision: cut inside towards the curvature and outward no more, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, put them back according to their natural form in their proper place, if you can, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the area below the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the area above the belly, then raise the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two areas, place your attention so that the wounded part is higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds apply what is prepared for you, then take one pitiful minister who wets all the rupture with his hand and brings together the lips; and this is the common method of suturing, which is that you take one needle or more according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' space from the head of the wound, and there stick a needle with good strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with the two edges of the siphac, which is beneath the skin inside, until it passes through that part, and bring together the two edges of the siphac all four together; then tie a double thread around the needle from both parts, then bring together both sides of the wound properly, and leave another finger's space, and stick another needle; then tie off the thread as you did with the first needle, and continue this according to your need for needles until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be of medium size; and it does not suit to push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so they do not damage and work the wound before healing; then cut off the points of the needles so they do not hurt the patient in sleep, and put bandages or cloths on the points of the needles to hold them firmly, and leave them until the wound is healed; this method of needle suturing is more suitable for small wounds, because it takes one needle or two. The second suture is common, which is that you bring together both sides of the skin and the two edges of the siphac all together with one needle with medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these four edges altogether, continue sewing from the part where you began in the way clothes are sewn; put a space between each stitch as wide as half a finger's thickness. This suturing is known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had on his stomach which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm long, and two palms of intestines were sticking out, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sealed up to 15 days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle, and pierce from the outer side to the inner; when it has gone through straight to the center, place the head of the needle where you have pierced with the needle, and make it penetrate again from the inner part to the outer; the purpose of this stitch is that you sew just as leather workers do with hides, leaving one surface aside once, then taking it up again so that the stitching may be fully completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen described precisely, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the surface to the other end in such a way: stick a needle at the head of the wound nearest, and pierce only that spot, leaving the two ends of the surface; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part up to the inner part, at the two ends of the surface; then pierce one and the other from the outer part up to the inner part, at two other heads of the wound which are on the opposite side; and this is the most used method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suturing is more severe than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgement of the wound is such as the judgement of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even though the fire has moved it, then reset the intestines, and the cut; then put on the healing powder to the flesh, and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present until the wound drinks; and sew the thread, and let the sides be soldered, and the membrane; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to throw off pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound may communicate with the principal members, then you must wet light wool in tempered oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in bowels, which often happens, then cleanse them with warm black wine, and likewise if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and pierce within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are wounded, and this is due to the abundance of veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of all the body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the hernia comes out of the wound, reset it as you would with an intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned green or black, then you must bind the area that has turned black so no further bleeding occurs, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the bindings, and hang both shoulders from the part below the wound up to above to ease the extraction when the hernia falls out and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and excretions and air came out; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until he was healed, and the opening was sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sealed, I feared that the patient might have problems in his belly; and there was no problem, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experienced people said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a way: take pins with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it over both edges so that it holds them tight; then cut off the head, and this stays so that it cannot come loose, then put another pin after it in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is covered; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Those heads burn inside the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the head of this intestine thread which is very thin, and then tie to the head of this intestine thread the fine linen thread tightly, then put the thread in the needle, and stitch the intestine, and repeatedly in the tear; and this way of sewing in the flesh is not other than according to the method of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no skill or knowledge, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	about the fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it awakens, is universally called "fistula", and especially when it is hairy and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a false nodulation hard and white, where there is no pain, and it is also hairy like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it discharges clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is only due to one of the nine causes: namely, by the scarcity of blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on the edges, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is porous, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption takes the form of a pestilence; or because the property of the region delays digestion, and health comes late, and it swells by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must make you know the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and there is such that comes to the principal part of the member and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have faith in its treatment, and you wish to recognize it, then take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, so seek it out; and if the fistula is curved, then search it with a fine probe of lead, for lead bends around the curvature; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot well explore it with probes, then irrigate it through one opening, for moisture thus flows from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then carefully seek it out as much as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and proceed with caution, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and the place where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have said, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the foulness and corrupted flesh that are inside; and then treat it until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply located straightly, you must cut thoroughly as much as you can, then place moistened probes in medicine with astringents inside, and push them to the head of the fistula so that the medicine corrodes the excess remaining at the bottom; and then apply salves for healing until it heals; and if it does not heal by this method, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not trouble you in the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape until all the corruption is removed, then treat with healing substances until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and begins to leak again as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: so expose and scrape until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other method but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with tongs, then pull it out with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving not one behind; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear, cut away both the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound something to encourage putrefaction, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then the bones will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then only let corruption reign until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupted part reaching to the marrow of the bone; you must saw and cut all the way to the corruption, then cure it until it heals; and I will tell you of an ulcer that happened to a man in his leg so that you take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was the young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, until the materials reached the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no clear reason to open; but the doctors by their foolishness worked so much on it that the abscess opened, and much material corrupted, and became an ulcer, and many openings developed from which all expelled pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors treated him for about two years, and there was no wise one in the art of hands until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what came out through the openings in large amounts; and the young man's body turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one came opposite the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the perforations until I uncovered part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced; the corruption extended to the inner bone; I sutured what appeared to be the corrupted bone and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and began to treat the wound with poultices for a long time, but it could not heal; then started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and sutured it, and then removed it, and tried to close the area; but I could only cut around a palm of the bone, and treated it without its whole mass, then applied medicine; and it was quickly healed and closed, and there was no need to begin work again except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation he often bled, but was entirely healed, and in place of the bone hard flesh grew, and was of good condition and had no harm nor contrary at all in any way, nor when going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sutured in this way: take a thread, and tie it at the end of the exposed bone, and command someone to pull it upwards; and put another thicker linen thread on top of the flesh that is over the bone, and extend the end so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh where you wish to sew, so that the needle does not hurt the flesh; and place a coal or a hot plate under the bone to help cut away the corrupted flesh; and one must suture as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and sew again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then place the hot iron below, and then saw from one side to the other of the corruption, and let the saw be as long as the length of the corruption, just as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the ankle of the foot, this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you must examine that corrosion how it appears to you; and clean it in all ways as you can, but without the vein or nerve opposing you; and know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance and thickness and subtlety and size and smallness and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare each kind of work its tool; and know that the work will show you the tool which you need according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool which you need according to what suits it.
dou feu	from the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder rots either from within or from deficiency; and when you have treated that corruption with medical remedies and they do not help, then it is necessary to amputate the limb up to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes death by this means, or from the evil, which is greater, of the loss of the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, the corruption spreads member to member, and takes over the whole body; so hasten to amputate, and if it is from the sting of venomous creatures such as sea scorpion and basilisk and similar, if the corruption is at the tip of the toe, cut it off, and do not give it time to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, death occurs, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its strength; and in this way do when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off all the foot; and if it rises up into the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to death; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie above and below, and have one minister hold one tie down, and another minister the other tie up, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties with a spatula wide enough so that the bone be uncovered; then cut or saw, and put on each side a linen cloth so that the saw does not touch the healthy area, and brings to the patient another injury and hot abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, then quickly cauterize the place or put on some binding powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to one man in his foot: he had a blackening that seemed like fire burning, and this corrosion first came on his toe of the foot, such that it would seize the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cut off the foot, and he was healed; and long after, the corruption returned at the finger of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on repellent things after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corruptions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the man’s strength was weak; and he completely despaired and returned to his land, and hurried to cut off his hand, and he was healed; and I have this story only so others do not act differently when they need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess occurs in fatty tissue and remains for so long that it gathers a great mass of pus; then it rots and bursts, and the pus comes out, and the place stays open like wounds; and the skin above is as thin as delicate linens, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called «sain», and is not called «fistula»; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, then it is called «fistula»; and you cut off all this skin around it, especially when it is thin like delicate linens; and one does not worry about its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear that the skin will corrupt, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clyster thus: look if the swelling is large, and the pus coming out has a foul smell, then clysterize it with Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take assafoetida, oil, and ceruse equally, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the swelling, and keep the opening closed; leave the medicine for two hours, then extract it by squeezing; do this many times until the swelling is cleansed, and the filth removed. Sometimes it is clysterized with ash water when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from vine wood, pour water over them, strain it, and use it as a clyster until you know that the swelling is well cleaned; if the patient cannot bear this, nor can they bear Egyptian medicine or ash water, then clysterize with water and honey in which there is a bit of ground ceruse mixed; or you may clysterize with honey and wine mixed, for honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and wine makes it burn; and when you have done this, if you believe the swelling is well cleansed, then clysterize what will cause flesh to grow in it, which means taking a diaphoretic plaster and mixing it with rose oil and wine; or you may clysterize with some medicines and ointments of which I have mentioned their properties in the chapter on ointments. If the opening of the swelling is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it a bit with an iron tool and put inside a piece of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened; if the wound is too large, sew it up leaving only one place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening that emits pus is at the top, cut it lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is perfect, it does not allow further meat growth; and if you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, prepare in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place possible, for when the pus is perfect, it does not allow further meat growth and if you cannot cut under the breast as you wish, prepare in such a manner: so that the pus runs lightly downwards and leaves nothing of the pus; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stretch over the linen cloth that covers all of the wound; then cut forcefully at the narrow part of the breast slightly wider than the first, then spread an ointment over another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the wound's opening to lighten the pus, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to clear away the pus, and know what runs from the pus, whether it is venom or little or much, or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain in a name (part), and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been thus extended and you see nature spring up over the opening of the wound, then know that the breast is healing already, and health approaches; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested bile after many days, know that the breast will not be cured.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle pus forms after a long time, do not despair of the health, for recovery approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people to whom the healing of flesh in their wounds takes time, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested bile flows from the breast after many days, know that the breast will not be cured; and if the breast delays in drying up and is swollen, apply moist substances with drying properties, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment, mix it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equally in substance; then cook it and use it; and the same goes for honey, which is better cooked when diaphoretic ointments are not present, or take myrrh and aloes and frankincense, grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue the cloth with it, and spread it over the breast, and sometimes aristolochia longa and roots of lilies celestial, which are also like wheat flour and chalk; use simple or compound substances: grind them, make a powder, put it over the honey I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has reached its peak and affects the bone or hard limbs or joints; treat it with fistula therapy, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps occurs in other fingers; and when it becomes old, and one does not take care, then comes the hot abscess, and it spreads and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it destroys it entirely; and the corrosion goes up to the bone, causing a foul pain, and the joint of the finger becomes swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off with an iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses on the flesh inside, and it begins to pain, and injures it, then you must put wax under the nail that pricks the flesh, and raise it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and apply medicines that burn and corrode on the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it and draw out, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see it needs to be corrupted, cut it with an I-shaped knife as was previously said, then treat it until it heals; and if it is swollen, protruding, and causing great pain, you must first alleviate it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile across, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the swelling of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocated joint that occurs in the hands of some men is entirely fleshy, and at times it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some are born at the root of the joint, or the origin is in some ways of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which is born in any knot of the finger does not move, and that which is born at the joint of the finger may move; the size of the fleshy one is slight, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which is born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat: be careful with cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born with a hemorrhoid, you must first cut the flesh roundly to the bone, then cut the bone at an appropriate line for that, then clean it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The syndromes that come to the hands together come by birth, or by wound union, or by fire burn, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that union so the fingers return to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or oiled rags that they do not unite; or you put between two pieces of fine linen until the joints are properly united.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the syndrome comes to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut that union as appropriate.
des vils	of the villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These are large veins filled with excessive melancholic humors that come to many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer a purge of bile to him, and then treat him with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut it and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure is as follows: first, wash the leg with very hot water until the thick blood is thinned, then strap the patient’s leg above the knee down to below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision, then lift and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's condition can bear; then tie it off, and instruct him to eat foods that engender black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full again, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of it is according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put him in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then cut straight along the vein from the long side to the head of the knee, or in the part below at the ankle; then work the skin with the lancet, and scrape the vein on both sides until it appears when you feel it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then put the needle under it until it is raised from the skin, and then cut it lightly with the lancet, then cut in another place three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the needle as you have done, and paint it with another lancet like you did first; then cut another piece, or several if you need to, then lift it, and cut at the toe, then pull and lift up to the second section; then draw it out from section to section until it comes out completely whole, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle with a very strong double thread in it, and tie and pull it, and put under it a needle, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out; and beware that it does not break, for if it breaks, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have completely drawn it out, put on the site of the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the skin is tight and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not chop it; and pull it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the skin is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of thick curvature, for if it were finer, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil war
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This war is generated in the legs, in hot areas where no grass or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and it may occur in other places besides the legs, and this happens due to the putrefaction that comes under the skin, just as serpents and worms come inside the body, generated between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a great inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the blood begins to flow out forcefully, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap around a piece of cloth from three and a half inches to two inches, tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time it comes out a little further, wrap it again around the cloth, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot in that place, a bad disease; therefore, it must be treated little by little until the end, leaving nothing in the body; sometimes this vein can be up to five palms long or ten when treated, and once a man came to me with one that was ten palms long. When you cut it, place one stake at its opening, pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out, and empty all the matter inside, then apply purifying medicine to prevent any rot for some days, then treat it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein has less redness, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or near the foot, and there comes much pus, from which it lacks redness; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cattle sickness" in our land because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, traveling all over the body up and down, and one can feel it well as it moves from member to member until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and comes out weak; and it arises from the corruption of certain humors, just as worms and serpents and earthworms and ascarides come in the belly; and there is concern about its malice, for when it travels through the body and climbs to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance entering, it can destroy the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you want to cure and draw it out, one cannot do so except when it moves: therefore, then you must bind the area above and below with a strong tie tightly, then cut up and draw forcefully, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then hold firmly below it the eyelid tightly, then cut up, and draw forcefully; and the patient must be treated with bodily purification by medicines that dissolve bad humors corrupting, and use foods that generate corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she exposed her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and right after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, as quicksilver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot, and fixed itself on the shoulder, and then shortly after ran throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it was now circling around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved so from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had wanted many that well they wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins uncovered, and for this reason this constrained wind appeared; and it does not appear according to this reasoning to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then apply something over and under quickly, and then cut so that the constrained wind issues from the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with what expels winds, such as foul pills, and pills of theriaca, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their forms and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity among them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with blades, and those with pieces; and the one that strikes any member does so in two ways: it strikes a principal member if it is barbed, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears: then you should refrain from extracting this arrow, for death often follows; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not embedded deeply, then extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls in and pierces the bone, and the outer membrane which is on the brain jumps, is when there is blindness and a flow and disorientation and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there flows out without strength from the nostrils or from the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and white moisture like flour jumps from the wound, and likewise brain matter like cooked meat; and if these signs appear to you, then hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it falls on the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like flour, and draws black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: then know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that is embedded in the throat is that without warning foam comes from the wound, and the neck swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the lung, it is near the ribs; and causes great anxiety and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance some undigested meat may come from the wound.
