Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and any hay comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out in fits, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the spine and the wrist and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the arm near the root of the nose: I probed it and drew it out from another side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out at once an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid below, and the arrow was embedded, and could not reach its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; the game was healed, and no ill accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with ears: I cut the barbs, and worked so subtly that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And draw out an arrow from the man who had it in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, he did not change his condition; I cut into the arrow, guided it, drew it out forcefully, and had no ill accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow struck on the back, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor found harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man to whom an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And extract an arrow from the man of the king's household, to whom it fell in the middle of the nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was entirely embedded. I was called for treatment after it had been three days since it fell.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I wanted to examine it with a subtle probe, and did not feel it; and he felt a sting and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I put on a binding and digestive plaster to prevent swelling; and the head of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained this way for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his chest; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a medicine with corrosive properties to the wound for several days until it was open, and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow embedded in the location; then I continued to treat the opening of the wound with that medicine until the tip of the arrow became visibly apparent; and it took about four months for this process to complete, after which I widened the wound sufficiently to insert tongs, moving them from side to side, but could not extract it; therefore, I did not stop trying various subtle methods and devising means of extraction until one day I grasped it with properly made tongs, as will be described at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	For I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you focus on what I do not say, for books cannot take everything into account; but wise masters compare well with little knowledge, and upon what is present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, to address the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not go out of the limbs where they are fixed except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or from another side; and those that come out through the place where they entered are arrows entering into their flesh, and sometimes coming out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be until the flesh around rots and the discharge is cleansed; and likewise if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it this way for some days, and move it each day; then it comes out, and if it still does not come out, pierce around it all the way to the core carefully, until the area around widens, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes to one of the brain's chambers, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned affect the patient: do not extract it, but leave it until it becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow comes to the surface, it is deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed only in the bone and does not come up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without bad incident, then do not attempt to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer tar around it as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the entire area; and if you feel it, then extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then widen the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it clings, then remove the flesh that is embedded in two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, for you would extract it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the area around is swollen, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood works against you, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and use ingenuity how you can pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot, then set him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where something of it is visible, or the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or clearly feel it: cut into it then, until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: now it has come out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then rotate your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it still and repeat the extraction until it comes forth; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, force all the shaft; and if the shaft falls off and you wish to administer further, use the hair instrument so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; then push hard, and if the arrow is barbed, use an instrument with a pointed end going in to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the flesh or on the belly or at the bladder or at the side, and it is near, and you can cut over it, do so cut; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers with which one extracts arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and you see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the hair pusher is also like the feather of a bird, to insert at the tip of the arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for inserting and squeezing is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	the veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, of which 16 are on the head: namely, two that are behind the ears, called the two "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the temples, visible; and the two veins that are in the tear ducts of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two jugular veins that are on the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips of the mouth, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly bled from are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it «vein of the head»; and the middle one is called «faste», and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it «vein of the heart»; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it «vein of the belly», and it is above the forearm, and it is the one that is bled from, which appears clearly on the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the elbow on the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called «nesse», which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The salting of veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraine; and the quality of the salting, as I tell you, is to raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then let the patient squeeze his neck in a fist, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending from the head: hold them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, make an incision; then take the lancet, and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, and cut both skin and vein well twice across, and let out blood as much as you wish; then tie it tight until it is stopped; and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The salving of the two arteries that are in the temples is good for old migraines, sores, and accustomed ophthalmia, and for tears that are watery in the eyes; and the quality of the salving is as I say: and it is that the patient strains his neck, until the two veins appear clearly; and feel the pulse under your finger, and then mark the spot; then lift up the skin over the vein with your index finger, and pierce with the lancet underneath, and raise the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done in the other two veins, and let blood according to your necessity; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; then tie it properly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the sickness of the cephalic for old diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness; and the quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digging tool", whose form is thus:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is clean and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the blades to be too sharp; and cut sideways, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the blade when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The salving of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with the eyes, and for dandruff, and redness, and the iris in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their salving is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting some part, as before; then he anoints it, and let the anointment be sideways, a bit along the length of the flame somewhat wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are delicate, they may break; then let blood as much as you need, and then bind on a cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The salving of the nose vein is good for water retention, and for stubborn sores, and for face ailments such as migraines and redness that comes on the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of the salving is such that the patient strains his neck, then draws out his nose with your left hand, and take a delicate long flame, and insert it between the two nostrils in the space there, for the vein does not open easily here, and the blood will start to flow; and do not go too deep, let blood according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two guindeges aids in the treatment of the alainne, and at the beginning of meselerie, and much of diseases, and for impetigo, and corrodens, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the salve is that the patient stretches his neck under one and then the other, as we have said; and let the master stand on the head of the patient, and the patient sit upon a chair, then open the vein a little broadly, then draw blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do likewise in the other vein, then release the tie, and bind both veins moderately so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve for the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The swelling of the veins of the upper lips aids in phlegm in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and of the nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the swelling is to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by their black color, and by the small black veins around them: cut both then, and if you do not recognize them and you are in doubt, then cut the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the swelling under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The swelling of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the swelling of the cephalic vein, and it is at the narrow part of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sweller is that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black vein: then cauterize one and the other, and do not go too deep, for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat that are usually cauterized are cauterized in two ways: with a sharp iron blade covered in mirtin oil or olive oil, just like cutting blades, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The first form of the flame mint is much renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the full and closed veins filled with thick and visible blood, which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and it is for healing the fine veins where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the back, and in the abdomen; and it is important for the surgeon to heal wisely, and to be careful of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes out, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking but cutting like a file.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, it is necessary to extract it and change to another; or you want any ray from it, or you incise a vein in its place on the arm: it opens clearly; and cut it with a file-like flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the incision, first you must bind the arm, touch the spot until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with a sign, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with a file-like flame; and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the spot swell, for it is from the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rise up like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: hasten then, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind his arm, and leave it so, and let not the patient move it; and he should be without fear, and do not move it until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop, and it overpowers you, and the medicines are not at hand, cut the artery if it is exposed, for the head of the retractors; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of fig, and split it, and take one half and bind it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping is not difficult in many positions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the binding on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The swelling of the vein in the middle helps it to draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to beware of the nerve that lies beneath, and if he pricks too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the patient becomes very ill, and perhaps cannot recover; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you must find it with an awl instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The swelling of the cephalic vein helps it to draw blood from the head and assists the eyes; and it is necessary for the surgeon to puncture it with olive oil or mirtum oil, because it is the safest of all veins, as there is neither a nerve nor an artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest site, and it does not matter if one misses the first time, and one starts again; and by chance the veins swell in some men when one misses the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it is not performed except to maintain health and to prevent future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins found in the arm: namely, cephalic, basilic, and median; and one should perform bloodletting at the beginning of spring, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and one should perform bloodletting on the first day or the third, two or three hours after the day has begun.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine that is administered to the illnesses has no set time, but when there is need by day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it does not befit to medicate children until fourteen years, nor a woman carrying life from the fourth month until seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not medicate those who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is fitting that they purge their intestines with a light enema if they have much bile retained so that the veins do not attract from the intestines the harmful superfluities detrimental to the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are overly sated with food, or who are drunk until sober, nor dropsical; and it is debated whether to bleed after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, labor, staying awake, and fasting, and whatever exhausts all strength, from weapon use or from the body; then refine the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then enter into the bath, unless something prevents it, to refine the blood, and be bled from the vein of the arm around the third hour as we have said; and guard that day against labor, pain, lust, and similar things; and be calm and joyful, and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and they rub the arm two or three times, then moderately tighten the ligature above, because when it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow; and then they rub the area with their hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then the bleeder moistens the flame of a small oil lamp old, then places their left hand on that vein below the spot where they wish to bleed so that the vein does not rise and fails when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like ropes in the surgeon, and there are such that are full of windiness, so when one puts on the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those; and if he works the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason, therefore the surgeons must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked the first time, it's good; if not, then begin again a little below that place or above quickly, if the place is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the place is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for one day or two, and do not loosen the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will come; do not enter the bath, then resume the surgery if she pleases; and if the opening is small, cut the blood carefully and you doubt that enough blood will flow, then apply the full flame directly to that opening; and work a little quickly, although the place may be swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin again the inflammation, and put on a pot of oil residue, for it lightens the body from blood, and is milder in this place the residue than the oil; and thus administer the oil residue in each inflammation that you heal the veins to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing does trilateral and bull's gall when one puts it on the place; so subtle is the blood and it disperses when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not treated strongly at the time when the opening of the vein is small, then you must hurry and put on the place a sponge soaked in water and salt one pot hot, and press for an hour; and you should do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if there remains any black or green color in the area after some days, it will not harm him; and if you see, put on some aloes or mastic dissolved in calamus juice, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appear at the joint of the shoulder: put then your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that swelling is evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Beware then that you do not put anything on what we have said, for perchance it may cut into the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, that a larger wound be made, and the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he must be bled little and often, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood flowing out and nerve severing, and is better than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body is lacking in bloodletting, it is necessary to give bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, then draw blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold complexion, then let him eat before bleeding bread soaked in musk syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the bleeding, after the flow of much blood, then it is necessary that he inhales broth of meat, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed one arm and bleed at other times, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little and a little, according to the amount of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to bleed one arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to heal on another side, must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated and causes fever; thus one must draw a large quantity and widen the opening until it flows freely; then when you restore all conditions of healing, and place your hand on his pulse while he bleeds, so death does not come instead of the blood flowing out, and this happens often when the healers are negligent; and it is not right when you wish to release the arm and let blood a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press forcefully upon it; nor if it is bent, should he extend his arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds a second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, until the frozen blood from the vein’s opening comes out, and put on the poultice of cloth soaked in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is need to bleed a second time, then bleed in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein at the head because it is composed that way.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the palm is red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, then bleed now across, not wide nor long; and let the puncture be wide, and bleed very close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, for it is placed there more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve of the palm of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: draw out the hand, and put it in hot water until the veins are swollen so that they can be seen; and if you cut crosswise, and if you cut entirely through, it will cause no harm; do not go too deep, for the nerves are all exposed beneath the skin, and then put the hand back into hot water if the sinew is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, put oil and seal on the vein to quickly close it, and do this for each incision.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve on the left hand is good for the disease of the spleen, and do everything as I have said for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of sophene is worth for all the diseases that are below the body, like diseases of the marrow, and retention of urine, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and of old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that the patient puts their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it softens, and apply it over the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot are many veins; then apply it to the widest vein or at the ankle, where it works best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it to the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and apply the salve across as well as when cutting; and let the flames be small.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein fully empty.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the bleeding fails the first time, then start again a little higher up, for the sinew is salty; do not worry about the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same with the other foot's wound.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The sinew of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its bleeding leads to pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient enters the bath and compresses above the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then bleed it in every way you can, including across; and it is better that you cut it off, for the sinew is salty, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, cut some vein on the back of the foot towards the little toe and be careful of the nerves; and let as much blood as you wish, then untie the ligature, put cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping is made from horns, or clay, or glass; and cupping treatment is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping treatment without striking is done in two ways: either with full fire or without fire; and the cupping that is done by striking and extracting blood is done at fourteen places on the body, of which one is at the very top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and a cupping under the chin; and a cupping on both shoulders; and a cupping on the buttocks; and cups in both arms; and cups on both legs; and cups on both ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, but only from the small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone as vein bleeding does; and it should not be administered, with full fire or without fire, in any disease caused by excess, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is needed to cup, or for customs, then we do so each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at every time; for there are such who, when they need to be cupped, have heavy head; and there are such who find fullness and redness on their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness before their eyes; and there are such who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are such who dream, and see at night blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order it to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The swelling of the temple thus helps with the dryness of the head … which affects the eyes, and it is not advisable that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the swelling of the cephalic, and it is not advisable for those who have a cold temperament to use it, or who have catarrh, because it does them much harm; and for this reason it is not advisable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become forgetful, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a little lower due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation on the neck is in place of the swelling of the head and the basilic, and for this reason it is useful for the constriction of the breast, and to split the channel of the nostril, and for all, and for fullness; and there should be a little pressure, because if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or nausea in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Windings around the second ribs of the neck are good for headaches, and ophthalmia and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of basilica salve; and you must instruct the surgeon to press his hand when applying, that he does not cut the artery, and there be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Windings under the chin are good for mouth diseases, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in place of salves for the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Windings on the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Windings on the ribs are as good as those on the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to strike too deeply, for the area is bare of flesh, and lies close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases below, and it must be large, and made of metal so that it can draw well; and by chance, if it were delicate, it would break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses on the legs draw openly, for they attract blood from throughout the body, and are good for old pains of the reins, and of the gallbladder, and of the bladder, and reset the flows; and they are in place of two sophenes, and of two ankles, and always they weaken the body after long use, and cause faintness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the ventouse is that you first place it empty, and suck moderately, and put it quickly, and move evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and swollen, and perceive the color of the blood; then rest, and reapply the ventouses, and be careful with the condition of the body, for there are those who have much flesh, and clear veins: so it is necessary to strike only once, and make large wounds, and a bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw the blood little by little, we only strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, then strike deeply, and the aim is that the veins be pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the sites of the cupping with opening and dissolving oil: if it is in winter, of violet oil, or almond oil, or squash seed oil; and if it is in summer, of watercress oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balm, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one heals someone with tender flesh and large pores, then no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of black nightshade, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, it is lifted with oil of asphodel, or water of myrtle, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those who have large excesses, they are treated with old wine, or water of juice, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and one should not heal with cupping before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath by one hour or two; and they should not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that they exercise when they are to be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is healing is choleric, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; then it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuces with oil, and similar things; and they should eat pulse, and meat of castrated animals, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold temperament should take honey syrup, and moderate wine, which is between old and new, and eat pulse, and pulse again, small birds, and pigeons; and on the day he will be bled, he must drink more than he eats; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes theriac or musk before or after bleeding, to strengthen the principal limbs; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The leeches that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the buttocks and the kidneys and the hip, because these limbs do not endure being pierced, and it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on the breasts when the child is nursing; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place leeches on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the limb; and removes pain when there is obstruction or stone, so by its attractive power it might remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus does it act when placed on the liver and spleen where there is retained windiness, and these leeches are administered empty just to suck; and sometimes they are used together with fire, and at other times filled with warm water, as in diseases of phlegm, and in such a way that one fills the leech with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and have on the side around the middle one small hole, as if to pierce a needle, and let it be of glass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and it should have in the middle a crossbar of glass or iron, to hold a burning ember, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping glass on the limb in the following way: take a burning ember of wax or linen, and put it inside the cupping glass through the bar that is in the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, with your fingers on the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor comes out, and remove the cupping glass; and apply the ointment as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there is no tube or opening, and it is not applied except when it is full of water, and it is placed only on the limb; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sponges are not applied except to limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and in bare parts of the flesh, such as toes or nails, and other similar ones; and the quality of use is that when you find sponges that are in clean sweet water without putrefaction, then take them; and place them for a night in sweet water until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their insides; and then if it has been bled from veins and suction cups, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply the sponges; and when they are full and fall off, if it is an area where suction cups can be placed, place a cup there, for this is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the area of ease, and then with water, very well, and then imprint it; and if the wound is too close to the body of the sinews, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put on, until the blood is stanchioned; and if the blood is multiplied, put on ground vitriol or gallnuts, and similar things, until it is stanchioned; or you put on the area half of peeled beans, and leave them until they burn at the place, it will stanch now; and if you need more, take other sinews.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sinews do not wish to take hold, then rub the area with fresh blood, or you stick a needle there until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they burn; and when you see that they fall, then powder on a bit of ground aloes and celandine, or ash, they will fall now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish physicians discard this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books nor read their letters; and for this reason knowledge is foreign in our land, for I have never found a good one. And I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I studied so much that I treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
