Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twist or crush comes to someone, then you must hurry to treat the patient on one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, or fainting, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and eat cool things, that is to say cold joints, and meat of fowl and veal, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill oneself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess, nor of material spreading in the limb; so that the patient returns to his first proper management which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with foods that produce great nourishment where there is viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the break repairs itself more quickly and better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and infirm people do not heal or mend well according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but it does not matter, reset the broken bone with thick tendons that hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and it does not complete all its work, and for this reason, it is necessary to nourish them with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go across, and others in sharpening, like the cut of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its method and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes into place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it is well revealed by swelling, and sounds when pressed by hand; and when there is no twisting nor sound on touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there may well be twisting, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it by hand, but apply medicines that come after here, and then bind it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes through and has two disjointed parts must now be set evenly, although abscesses may come; and if hot abscesses come, then leave it for some days until the abscess is calmed; then set it equal to the movement as you can lightly and wisely, and know that its restoration is lighter than those with pieces; then bind it as it should be afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in pieces, then stretch it from two parts, whether hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you must reset all additions in their places as much as you can move them, and be careful that no injury or pain comes to the patient from your work; and align well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: then raise it gently, and do not tighten too much, nor press as those who by their work cause a hot abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set, well instruct the patient not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not set right, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that no twisting comes when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar: it is fitting to wrap with soft and fine linen cloths; and those which are large, such as thighs and shins: it is fitting to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bands embrace all of the large limb, and constrain equally on all sides, so that there is no flaw; then tie around small padding, three or four times according to the limb, and press your hand somewhat throughout the bandage, then go above the break and press less, so that the break may move slightly away from the break; and soften the bandage little by little, until you reach a large part of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and turn around again over the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and press moderately, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first section above; then place between the bandages linen padding or cloths, so that it is all equal, then tie everything on top with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing for the abscess that is warm and which reduces the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then apply to your instruments, and they should be half the width of a reed carefully chosen, or made from wood used for shields, or palm ribs, and they should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint which one places on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as suits the size of the limb, whether small or large; then apply the splints just as you did in the first binding, then bind over with thread appropriately, as in the first binding on the fracture; narrower is afterwards, then less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like I have seen in the works of fools who make their bindings with twisted hemp ropes, and this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the arrows after they are embedded in their flesh, put under them tow of linen, or shredded wool, so that it does not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the skin is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to extract all broken limbs of arrows on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to insert arrows until five or seven days later, or longer according to your certainty of a hot abscess ensuing; and here is the method of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to the mill walls, and knead it with plenty of eggs, and apply this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in many cases, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the torsion: take З abareis and ladanum and endive and asafoetida and gum arabic and myrtle, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana V З.; alcohol IX З.; and make powder, and mix them with egg white; if the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and is good for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for torsion: take myrtle and marshmallow, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana IX З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bole X З., and grind well, and cook with water or egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones dislocated from their places, and to soothe the pain arising, and for cutting into the bone, and for fractures: take new wool, and mix it with oil and cooked fat, and place it on the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth apple leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chicory, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, one part of each; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making a stronger plaster than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of chicory, and flaxseed, balaustine, melilot, and succory, and flowers of violets and chamomile, one part of each; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb to restore strength anything other than a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between two neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says one should put on the broken limb to restore dry things a bit warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of poultice that is good for injury and pain: take goat's fat and human nails chopped up, or bird feathers, and mallows, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you loosen it a little after, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not loosen it for several days And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; and take light cloth, and sea sponge wet, and dip in water, and lift the area with it, until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it up overnight, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and calm the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the fine binding, and a little plaster, and do not squeeze it so tightly as before; and be gentle until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen has been entirely removed, and you need plaster and binding, then restart it as you have done before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the limb, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture heals, and the flesh grows over the joint; then restrain it more than before, and fatten its flesh as I said before; and if you see the area drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; then moisten it with warm tepid water every time you release it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work the nourishment goes to the limb, and quickly mends what the foolish doctor does wrongfully: it is bad, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing else but leaving it and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various manners of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are there, and diverse forms, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the neck removes all the bone down to the surface which is beneath the bone, just as an ax does to wood; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "hatching".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wounds of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a split from the edge of a stone, or from falling on a stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a penetrating fracture, which approaches up to the tissue that is under the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And there is a wound that penetrates the bone as fine as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and such a wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it makes a piece of the bone go inwards, and the place twists like how blacksmiths hammer on cauldrons; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have moist bones on the head, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these kinds of fractures that small fragments are separated like stars; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all sorts of fractures by cutting into them, and by probing attempts, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is understood by this, that when the bone is exposed and rubbed upon, the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, beware of the patient's accidents, and if you see any harmful signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stiffness, paleness, ague fever, eyes coming out forcefully and reddening, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no astonishing accident and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the tissue under the bone be corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture extends to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in this way: take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the site of the wound more thoroughly than you can. If bleeding occurs when uncovering the bone or if there is a warm abscess, help it with what is necessary, which means filling the area with cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the warm abscess calms down and the bleeding stops. Then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut with a narrow incision first, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various numbers of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of Indian iron; and work lightly so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, then you must pierce around it, either by making cuts with trepans, but be careful that they do not penetrate beyond the skull bone, and there should be a margin or circle at the tip to prevent it from passing through the bone; and you must have several so that each comes into place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepans for all skulls; and this is the form of the three types of trepans:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put the awl on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the awl to another part a bit after, and so do all around, then cut with the chisels the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you bring out the bone in your hand, or with any of the tools that you have such as tongs, pliers; and take care not to touch the brain nor the surface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, then it is necessary to remove the roughness that remains of the bone with another instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be finer and more subtle than other chisels; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with the tools; then clean the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is more secure; and he praises it greatly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone where the fracture shows movement, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incisor, of which here is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is angled on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet, so that you lightly saw through the entire bone, and be careful of the tissue beneath; if it is close to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the skin, and the bone is only cut on top, and there are small fragments, then it is necessary to address that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various sizes, to apply in each place most appropriately, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	And scrape first with large scrapers, and then with finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cutting and fine fractures, you must treat according to its orientation; and this is something that is not easily answered by one who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the surface is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double-layered or triple-layered cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not press the surface too much, then apply another layer on top without binding it tightly except enough to cover the wound; and leave it thus for one or two days until the inflammation is calmed down, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, meal of vetches, incense powder, aristology, and similar things; and make a powder from these items, and put it on the wound, then immediately apply non-irritating medicines; and ensure that the wound remains clean, do not leave any ointment, nor allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's fabric, it corrupts and harms it, causing great harm to the patient; for when you place something corrosive on the surface, it rots over.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackening does not come except because of the medicine that has been applied, which has such virtue, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue one cloth, and put it on the surface; then treat it in the ways of treatments that are necessary until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, nor does it cause to bend or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must put your little finger in the hole of the nose, and place that break inside with your index finger, and press gently, until the nose returns to its natural form; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the fingers cannot reach the place, then you must make it even with the tip of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then repair it similarly, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation has calmed down, then put a linen cloth over the tip of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you place one against the other where the fracture is; and let the threads be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some say that one should moisten the threads with butter and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened with egg white and powder of mill; then leave the thread until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is stiffened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose quills in the nose instead of threads, and wraps a cloth around it, and if the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through; do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, put a poultice or cotton moistened with rose oil, or with a drop of mercury.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses do not come, apply a plaster made of powdered flaxseed and frankincense mixed with egg white, then place light bandages on it, and do not bind the nose; and if the fracture of the nose is small and broken into pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound, and treat it with things that heal flesh and promote healing, such as plasters and suitable ointments; and if there is no wound inside the nose, cure it with tents, and place linen strips in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured below, and there is no open wound, and the break is only superficial, and is not split into two, but rather indented inward, it is recognized as a minor injury.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your index finger in the patient’s mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, then use your right hand's index finger, and push the fracture inward slightly, and align it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two, it is necessary that you administer extension from both parts until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs or fracture, then extract them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw cerate, and put on the cloth double; and put on the cloth a large well-made plate or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed; and put a plaster on, of the powder from the mill with egg white or flaxseed flour, after you have removed the cerate; and put on the plaster light wool, and if the plasters dry out, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, repair it if no piece of the bone has been removed; then use appropriate instruments to remove any fragments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is wide, and apply appropriate poultices to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks often before, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners: when it is broken and separated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the break is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the forcele is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put equal the break in your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no appearance nor misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, then place under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or of wool, and let it be large according to your necessity; and extend and lift the arm, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you put equal the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back into place due to its being stuck, then it is necessary for the patient to lie often on his side, and put under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the attendant push the shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, you must cut above; pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, cut it with one of the incisors that you have; but place this instrument under the shoulder to protect the skin.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not closed, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and let it have two heads, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound that you made when pulling the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the opening is small, or you fear a hot abscess, apply cloths and bandages to the wound according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, moisten the cloth with rose oil and with asses' fat and with wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and egg white, and put light bandages on, and place a sphere under the splint if you need; then take a very large band two palms wide, then put the double cloth over the bandages and the plaster; then take a slender stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy splint, and under the sick splint; and hold from each side, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the bands loosen, then tie them again; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small bolster under the splint when he sleeps to lift the shoulder up; this will lighten the fracture by lightening the force of the arm, or you bind his arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents come, until twenty days; then restart the plaster if you see that it is needed, and hold it like this until it is restored; and it is restored in most cases within twenty-eight days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that the shoulder is broken at its wide part or in the middle, and one does not know it except by touch; then set it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in every way you can; then put powder from the mill with egg white on the area, and light bandages, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide and thin board slightly larger than the shoulder, and if under the board there is any unevenness at some point of the shoulder, use fine flaxen tow to make the board sit evenly; then tightly bind it with a large strap so that the board does not move from its position, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten it, and reset the board if it moves from its place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five, and when this number of days is completed, then release the binding, and be sure, for it is not bone that shifts easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points below the heart, cut above it, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the arm to ease an abscess that is hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the hip
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the top.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain, lacks strength, becomes faint, and may vomit blood, and the marrow appears in the broken bone, which can be clearly seen.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders. Then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs from two sides with your hands, carefully aligning it equally in all ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over a thin layer of salt or another light wood on top, wrap it in a cloth, and place it directly on the broken bone so that it does not move. Then turn the binding around to the back, tightly secure it, and retie the bandage every hour if it becomes loose; if it loosens, tighten it again. If it needs to be undone for corrosion or itching, pain, or abscess that comes to the area, do so quickly, undo it, remove the plaster, address what has occurred with treatment methods; then reapply the plaster and bind it until healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs only occurs in their thick parts behind the back, and at the head inward, and they only bend because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination with the hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is to set the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is inclined inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, like pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and they have sharp pains, and quickly vomit much blood, which is a sign of severe illness, and the ancients put much ingenuity into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And so there are some who say that one must administer foods that inflate the belly, to push the wind downwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not wish for hot abscesses to occur if they have not already appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has occurred, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we apply cupping to the area to bleed thoroughly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cupping may draw the excesses to the area due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the warmth around, then treat it with the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, then one must cut above the site of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument underneath to protect the surface; and then one should cut the bone, pull gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then place cloths soaked in rose oil on the area; and treat the site as appropriate for an abscess, and let them lie often on their side where it should be until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the break occurs to the neck bones, and it often happens that it bends; and similarly with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then beware if you see his hands softened, swollen, and lifeless, and he cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are squeezed and pricked, know that the bone’s joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then beware if the legs are softened, and if the symptoms that appear in the hands are present, and on the back there is flatulence and involuntary discharge; and when it is examined on its stomach, there is involuntary discharge.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to saddle up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: do not labor too much in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply it if there is a hot abscess, put rose oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then put one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cut above the heart; remove the bone, then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with healing ointment until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the skull," place your left hand pouch on it, and equalize it to the other side as much as you can, then apply the plaster and the splint if needed; then bind it tightly, and if there are dislocated bones, cut into them, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction at the top; and it causes lengthening, and tilting outward, and the patient feels pain in the area, and numbness, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it until you are above the fracture; and you know what the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then align that fracture so that it returns to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it tilts inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is aligned for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then put on the plaster, then place a board of wood or horn over it, and bind tightly so that it does not move; and fill the space underneath the ribs until the swelling is leveled.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses come, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are calmed, and put on what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and bind it as appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a stick of medium thickness, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two bindings, and raise them up, and have the patient sit on a chair; then place his broken arm on the stick until it reaches the armpit, and in the middle make a wooden support, then attach it to something heavy or have an assistant pull down; then the doctor places the fracture even between his hands until the bone returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that the patient is placed on his back, and his hand is tied to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below all the way to the joint, and each stretches their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish that the extraction be stronger, then hold the limb below the fracture and above the fracture, and stretch each of the assistants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place one bandage under the armpit, and another towards the side, below the fracture; and likewise if the fracture is towards the side, it must be placed lightly, without effort, until the fracture is leveled on its place, and on the side; then set the break evenly as it should be, and hold it tightly, unless warm abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if warm abscesses come, then do not hold it tightly until seven days, and place wool soaked in ashes and rose oil on it until the warm abscesses are calmed; then hold it tightly, and the way to hold it is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm against the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and hold it tight against the aid, and against the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, then use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one inch of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fractured area three times on each side; then draw tight over the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the fracture, tighter and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the arrangement of the splints and the tightening as we have said, at the hour when you restore the broken limb, and you fear an abscess is hot, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then check every three days on the bandage to ensure that no itching or swelling comes in the place, or nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is directed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, do not untie it until after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion filled evenly with wool, and check every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor are the ligaments softened; direct it by the power of medicine, and give him the food we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be reset in forty days altogether; and then one must untie it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to properly direct the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and embedded, it remains to untie for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "forearm bones," of which one is small, and it is the one that extends to the wrist; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large forearm bone is broken, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small forearm bone is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fragment that is merely broken, then it should be gently extended and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fragment, then it should be pulled more strongly; and extend it on the cushion, and raise the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross over himself, and place the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or at the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then the doctor should place it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, then place each in its place, and if any detached piece pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut into it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the saw for wounds, I have spoken of it in a specific chapter; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the healing process an abscess occurs, apply a cloth with a salve made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and bind the cloth gently on top until the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the salve, and apply a poultice of mill powder with egg white, then place the strips, and let the strip of the fracture be stronger and slightly wider than the others; and know that there should be six strips on the arm in various arrangements: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and press more on the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as it moves away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths placed over the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread used for binding be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must spray the limb with warm water, until the itchings are calmed; and let the limb rest not tightly.
